### 2026-06-16 — T3.21 Blocker 2 (protocol half): per-IP throttle on the raw telnet/WS pre-auth login loop — *drop t321-preauth-throttle*
Closed the unshipped half of T3.21 Blocker 2 (the discovered follow-up under `7a4f4ee`). The PORTAL login path was already per-IP throttled (`web_portal._login_rate_ok`, 10/60s), but the raw protocol login loop in `game_server.handle_new_session` — fed verbatim by BOTH transports (telnet `_telnet_read_loop` and the public web port's WebSocket `{"input": ...}` channel) — was not. `db.authenticate`'s lockout is PER-ACCOUNT (5 fails / 5 min), so credential-stuffing ACROSS many accounts from one socket, and spamming `create` to burn bcrypt CPU on the shared event loop, were both unbounded.
- **`server/session.py`:** new `Session.client_ip` field (default `"unknown"`), captured at the transport seam.
- **`server/game_server.py`:** module-level `_preauth_rate_ok` / `_preauth_attempts` / `_reset_preauth_throttle` — one shared per-IP sliding-window bucket (10/60s, reusing `api._sliding_window_allow`) gating BOTH the `connect` and `create` branches BEFORE any DB / bcrypt work. Throttled attempts get a wait-and-retry message and never reach `authenticate()` / `create_account()`. The `"unknown"` sentinel (capture failure only — a live socket always has a peername) is exempt → fails open on the rare capture error and never couples unrelated callers through one bucket.
- **`server/telnet_handler.py`:** captures the raw, un-spoofable TCP peername (`writer.get_extra_info("peername")[0]`).
- **`server/web_client.py`** (production aiohttp WS): captures the client IP via the spoof-resistant `api._get_client_ip(request)` (honors X-Forwarded-For only from a configured trusted proxy).
- **`server/websocket_handler.py`** (standalone, non-prod): captures `websocket.remote_address[0]` for parity.
- `__token_auth__` deliberately left unthrottled (cheap HMAC verify, not a credential-stuffing vector; the legit web auto-login handoff fires exactly once).
- No schema change, no faucet/sink, era-clean. `tests/test_t321_preauth_throttle.py` (12: limiter admit/block/reset/per-IP/sentinel-exempt + seam-wiring asserts + end-to-end against the real login loop — 11th connect from one IP rejected without reaching `authenticate`, a different IP unaffected, a legit single login still authenticates). Gate green single-process.

### 2026-06-16 — T3.21: read-only SELECT connection pool (DB scale ceiling) — *drop t321-read-pool*
Brian decision #3 (2026-06-16, "do not defer — need it now"). The DB ran ALL queries through a single shared aiosqlite connection (`db/database.py`), serializing every read behind every write + the 1 Hz tick — the dominant scale ceiling the T3.21 audit named. Adds a **read-only connection pool** for SELECT-heavy read endpoints, leaving the single writer connection for writes (WAL already enabled, so readers see a consistent snapshot concurrently with the writer).
- **`db/database.py`:** lazy pool (built on first read, under an `asyncio.Lock`) of `SWMUSH_DB_READ_POOL` (default 4) connections opened **`mode=ro` + `PRAGMA query_only=ON`** — they are *physically incapable of writing*, so this path **cannot corrupt the DB** (the stated risk). New `read_fetchall` / `read_fetchone` + a `_reader()` acquire/return context manager. Env-var pool size (read at build time) is **boot-order-safe** — `load_tunables()` runs after `connect()`, so a tunable would freeze to its default. `:memory:` DBs (per-connection) fall back to the writer. `close()` tears the pool down (sets a `_closed` flag first; nulls `self._db` → idempotent double-close).
- **`server/web_portal.py`:** the read-only portal API (directory / profile / scenes / stats / me) routed from `self._db.fetchall` → `self._db.read_fetchall` (8 sites + the `_fetchone` helper). Writes (none in this API) untouched.
- **Hardening (from an adversarial code-review pass):** partial-build failure now closes the already-opened connections (no fd leak); `_reader` raises cleanly on a shutdown race (pool nulled mid-acquire) and won't return a connection to a discarded pool; `_ensure_read_pool` refuses to rebuild after `close()`.
- **Verified:** new `tests/test_t321_read_pool.py` (9 — read-correctness over WAL, read-only enforcement [INSERT raises], concurrency past pool size, lazy-build, env-var size, `:memory:` fallback, post-close raises, double-close safe, routing guard) + portal N1 fake updated for the new method + admin-audit/portal/boot-smoke regression (58 green). No schema change; behavior-preserving for reads.
- **Files:** `db/database.py`, `server/web_portal.py`, `tests/test_t321_read_pool.py` (new), `tests/test_portal_characters_n1.py`, `CHANGELOG.md`, `TODO.json`.
T3.18 (Ground UX overhaul) tail — the last deferred G3 cosmetic item. Client-only (`static/client.html`), zero engine-touch.
- **Far-room dimming.** The legacy `renderAreaMap` path (fallback when no AreaGeometry covers the room) previously rendered all rooms at full opacity. Added `rm-far` CSS class (`.rm-far .rm-dot { opacity: 0.38 }` / `.rm-far .rm-label { opacity: 0.3 }`) for rooms that are neither the current room nor an adjacent (clickable) room. In JS, the `if (isYou) … if (isAdj)` double-push is now `if (isYou) … else if (isAdj) … else push('rm-far')` — mutual exclusion guaranteed.
- **Per-move fade-in.** `renderAreaMap` now sets `svg.style.opacity = '0'` before clearing the SVG, rebuilds, then calls `requestAnimationFrame(() => svg.style.opacity = '1')` — the CSS `transition: opacity 0.12s ease-in-out` on `#g-area-map-svg` then cross-fades the rebuilt map in smoothly on every move.
- **7 new tests** (`tests/spa/test_g3_area_map_polish.py`): rm-far dot + label opacity CSS; SVG transition CSS; renderAreaMap assigns rm-far; else-if mutual exclusion; opacity-to-0 before clear; requestAnimationFrame restore. Smoke + hygiene green.

### 2026-06-16 — T3.21 SECURITY: close the unauthenticated `__token_auth__` auth-bypass (Opus loop) — *drop t321-token-auth-bypass*
T3.21 security pass. **Critical, unauthenticated full-account-takeover closed.** The web-chargen auto-login handoff used a synthetic command `__token_auth__ <account_id>` fed into the shared `handle_new_session` login loop; the branch *trusted* that web_client.py had already verified a token and simply did `get_account(int(parts[1]))` → login, no password. But BOTH transports feed RAW client input into that same loop verbatim — Telnet via `_telnet_read_loop` → `feed_input`, and the **public web port** via the WebSocket `{"input": "..."}` channel → `feed_input`. So any unauthenticated client could send `__token_auth__ 1` and seize account #1 (sequential ids = trivial enumeration) with no credentials.
- **Fix — the `__token_auth__` branch is now the authoritative verifier.** Its argument is the HMAC-signed login token (not a bare id); it calls `verify_login_token(parts[1])` itself and only authenticates on a genuine, unexpired token. `verify_login_token` is total (never raises; `None` on any malformed/expired/forged token), so a forged or guessed argument simply fails to auth. (`server/game_server.py`)
- **Producer aligned.** `server/web_client.py` now feeds the signed token straight through (`__token_auth__ {token}`) instead of resolving it to an account_id first — one trust point, and removes a redundant DB round-trip. The token is whitespace-free so `line.split()` preserves it; the SPA's legitimate post-chargen / "open in web" handoff is unchanged.
- **Blast radius confirmed contained:** exactly one producer (web_client) and one consumer (game_server); no SPA/static or test referenced the synthetic command. Stateless token verify = no double-consume concern. No schema change, no faucet/sink, era-clean.
- **15 tests** (`tests/test_t321_token_auth_bypass.py`): verifier rejects bare-id/garbage/tampered-sig and accepts a genuine token; both call sites wired correctly; **end-to-end against the real login loop** — a forged `__token_auth__ <id>` does NOT authenticate (session stays CONNECTED, `_character_select` never runs) while a server-minted token does. Smoke foundation (boots the server, drives the telnet/WS login) green.

### 2026-06-16 — T3.21 admin-audit trail for +home/+shop admin umbrella forwards (Opus loop) — *drop t321-umbrella-admin-audit*
T3.21 Blocker 3 follow-up. The dispatcher (`CommandParser._execute`) writes an `admin_audit` row for every BUILDER/ADMIN command that passes its access gate, but the PLAYER-level umbrella forwards `+home admin …` and `+shop admin …` call the ADMIN command's `execute()` **directly** — bypassing the dispatcher seam. The privilege re-check (`check_access`) was already wired in (the `9ca0692` escalation fix), but the matching audit write was missing, so an admin exercising power through the umbrella left **no trail**. Closed the hole.
- **Audit logic lifted to module scope.** `parser.commands.audit_privileged_invocation(cmd, ctx)` + `_redact_audit_detail(cmd_key, args)` are now module-level functions; the dispatcher's `_execute` gate, the umbrella forwards, and the back-compat instance shims (`parser._audit_privileged` / `parser._redact_audit_detail`) all share **one** implementation. No duplicated `record_admin_action` call site.
- **`+home admin` and `+shop admin` now audit.** After `check_access` passes and `ctx.args` is set, both umbrella `_admin` forwards call `audit_privileged_invocation(cmd, ctx)` before `execute()` — so `+home admin evict <player>` / `+shop admin …` leave the same `admin_audit` row (`command="@housing"` / `"@shop"`, redacted detail) a direct `@housing` / `@shop` would. The audit fires only after the access gate, so a denied non-admin still records nothing.
- **Scope verified.** A working-tree `check_access(ctx)` grep confirms housing + shop are the **only two** in-command privilege re-checks (umbrella forwards into a privileged command); no other audit-bypass seam exists. Secret redaction (`@newpassword` etc.) and the 500-char detail cap carry over unchanged.
- **10 new tests** (`tests/test_t321_umbrella_admin_audit.py`): module-helper presence + shim/module redaction parity + length cap; module func writes a row; instance shim still writes (back-compat); `db=None` no-op; `+home admin`/`+shop admin` as admin → exactly one audit row with the right command/detail; as non-admin → blocked, zero rows, permission message. Existing 20 `test_t321_admin_audit` cases still pass. No schema change. No faucet/sink. Era-clean.

### 2026-06-16 — T3.21 soft-endpoint per-IP throttle: unauthenticated check-name + validate (Opus loop) — *drop t321-soft-endpoint-throttle*
T3.21 security tail. The expensive account-creating chargen writes (`/api/chargen/submit`, `/api/chargen/create-character`) were already behind the strict per-IP limiter, but the two unauthenticated chargen *read* endpoints that still do real work on every call were unthrottled. Closed that gap with a separate, more lenient per-IP sliding-window limiter applied before any DB/CPU work.
- **`GET /api/chargen/check-name/{name}` throttled.** World-reachable with no token, it does one DB round-trip per call (and is a name-enumeration oracle). Left unbounded, a single client could flood it to enumerate character names or amplify load on the shared aiosqlite connection (which serializes every query in the process). Now `_check_soft_rate_limit(_get_client_ip(request))` runs *before* the DB query → the throttled call performs no DB work. The 429 body deliberately omits a matching `name`, so the SPA (which only updates its availability hint when `d.name === the typed name`) silently ignores it. The SPA's name-check is debounced 500ms after typing stops, so a legitimate user never reaches the limit.
- **`POST /api/chargen/validate` throttled.** Unauthenticated and CPU-bound (registry validation); not even called by the current SPA but live and floodable. Now throttled per IP before the body is read.
- **Separate soft bucket.** `_soft_rate_limits` / `SOFT_RATE_LIMIT_MAX=60` / `SOFT_RATE_LIMIT_WINDOW=60s`, distinct from the strict create bucket (`_rate_limits`, 3/60s) so heavy name-checking can't burn a legitimate user's create budget. Refactored the limiter into a generic `_sliding_window_allow(bucket, ip, max, window)` helper; `_check_rate_limit` (strict) and `_check_soft_rate_limit` (soft) are thin wrappers — strict behavior is byte-identical. Both key on the existing spoof-resistant `_get_client_ip`.
- **8 new tests** (`tests/test_t321_soft_endpoint_throttle.py`): under-limit 200 shape; 429 after the soft limit; throttled call does NOT query the DB; 429 body omits matching name; validate 429 + runs before body read; soft bucket independent of the strict create budget; per-IP isolation; window-prune re-admit. The existing 24 chargen-endpoint tests still pass (shared harness intact). No schema change. No faucet/sink. Era-clean.

### 2026-06-16 — Guide_09_CP_Progression.md accuracy fix: stale tick/cap constants + same-room kudos (Sonnet loop) — *drop guide-09-cp-progression-fix*
PRELAUNCH.help_guides_rework — Guide_09 corrected four stale values that were updated in v23 of the CP engine but never propagated to the guide. No engine behavior changes; the engine constants were already correct.

- **WEEKLY_CAP_TICKS 300→400** (guide §2 + §7): Guide said "weekly hard cap of 300 ticks (max 1 CP/week)"; engine runs at 400 ticks cap → max 2 CP/week.
- **PASSIVE_TICKS_PER_DAY 5→10** (guide §2 Source 1): Guide said "5 ticks/day"; engine `PASSIVE_TICKS_PER_DAY = 10` since v23. Passive total corrected from "~35 ticks/week = 1 CP every 8.5 weeks" to "~70 ticks/week = 1 CP every ~3 weeks".

Bullet replaced with accurate statement.

### 2026-06-16 — T3.21 admin-command access-gap fix: @housing/@shop privilege-escalation + umbrella check_access bypass (Opus loop) — *drop t321-admin-access-gaps*
T3.21 security tail (AccessLevel-enforcement audit). Built the full command registry exactly as `game_server` does (339 commands) and audited every `@`-namespace command's declared `access_level`, plus swept every PLAYER umbrella that forwards into another command's `execute()`. Found four gaps across two vuln classes and closed them; added a guard test pinning the convention so the class can't regress.
- **`@housing` (AdminHousingCommand) privilege-escalation — FIXED.** Shipped with **no `access_level`** → inherited `BaseCommand`'s default `PLAYER`, so any logged-in player could run the admin housing verbs: `@housing list` / `@housing inspect <player>` (enumerate + view every player's housing record) and **`@housing evict <player>` (force-evict any player)**. Gated to `AccessLevel.ADMIN`, matching the other player-state admin verbs (`@city`/`@bond`). `parser/housing_commands.py`.
- **`+home admin` umbrella bypass — FIXED.** The PLAYER-level `+home` umbrella forwarded into `AdminHousingCommand().execute()` **directly**, bypassing the dispatcher's `check_access` gate — so even an ADMIN gate on `@housing` would still have leaked through `+home admin evict <player>`. The `_admin` forward now re-runs `check_access` and denies non-admins before forwarding. `parser/housing_commands.py`.
- **`+shop admin` umbrella bypass — FIXED (same vuln class).** The PLAYER-level `+shop` umbrella (`admin` in `valid_switches`) forwarded into `AdminShopCommand().execute()` directly, so any player could run the ADMIN shop verbs (`@shop list`/`inspect`/`remove`) via `+shop admin <args>` even though `@shop` itself is correctly ADMIN. The `_admin` forward now re-runs `check_access`. Swept all other umbrella forwards (combat/space/espionage/faction/medical/places/builtin) — every other forward target is a PLAYER command; housing + shop were the only two that forwarded into a privileged command. `parser/shop_commands.py`.
- **`@getattr` (GetAttrUCommand) aligned to BUILDER — FIXED.** Shipped at `PLAYER` while its write/list siblings `@setattr`/`@lattr` are `BUILDER`. User-defined attributes are the builder namespace (room hooks `AENTER`/`ALEAVE`/`ADESC`, weather, custom messages); a player can't `@setattr` them, so there is no player read use case and reading a room's hook action strings leaks builder logic. Now `BUILDER`. `parser/attr_commands.py`.
- **Guard test (`tests/test_t321_admin_command_access_invariant.py`, 12 tests):** builds the live registry and asserts every `@`-command declares `access_level >= BUILDER` except a minimal explicit allowlist (`@desc`, `@mail` — genuine player self-commands, themselves asserted to stay PLAYER); an AST drift guard scans `parser/*.py` for `key="@..."` classes and fails if any is absent from the audited registry; behavioral tests confirm a non-admin is denied through both `+home admin` and `+shop admin` while an admin is forwarded, and `@housing.check_access` denies non-admins / allows admins. No schema change. No new faucet/sink. Era-clean.

### 2026-06-16 — T3.21 input-validation sweep: type/length bounds on chargen + portal POST bodies (Opus loop) — *drop t3-21-input-validation*
T3.21 security tail (MEDIUM). The unauthenticated chargen/portal JSON endpoints assumed the parsed body and several fields were well-typed; a malformed body crashed handlers with an unhandled `AttributeError`/`TypeError` (→ opaque 500) or wrote an unbounded blob into a character's `description`. All fixes are behavior-preserving for well-formed input. No schema change.
- **Non-dict top-level body → clean 400, not 500.** `server/api.py handle_submit` + `handle_create_character` and `server/web_portal.py handle_login` now reject a non-object JSON body (array/string/number/null) before any `data.get(...)` call. `validate_chargen_submission` also guards `isinstance(data, dict)` at the top, so `POST /api/chargen/validate` returns a graceful error list instead of raising.
- **Non-string field types never raise.** `validate_character_name` (non-str → "Name must be text.") and `validate_account_fields` (non-str username/password) guarded — they were called *before* the handlers' try-blocks, so a numeric `name` or list `username` previously 500'd at `len()`/`.strip()`/`re.match()`.
- **`background` coerced + capped to `MAX_BACKGROUND_LEN` (2000, the engine description norm).** Both char-build paths truncate `background` before it becomes `Character.description` — an unauthenticated `/api/chargen/submit` could otherwise store a ~256 KiB description (bounded only by the request-size cap). Mirrors the existing `chargen_notes[:2000]` seam.
- **Account password upper bound** (`MAX_PASSWORD_LEN = 128`) added at account creation (login unaffected; bcrypt only consumes 72 bytes). Non-dict `character` sub-body in the chain path coerced to `{}` so the force-sensitive probe can't `.get` on a non-dict.
- **Non-string `chain_id` rejected with 400** (code-review catch): an unhashable `chain_id` (list/dict) fed `corpus.by_id().get(chain_id)` → `TypeError` → 500. Guarded before the lookup.
- **15 new tests** (`tests/test_t321_input_validation.py`): validators never raise on malformed input, password bounds, non-dict login body → 400, non-string chain_id → 400, source-level guard + background-cap assertions at every seam. Regression sweep (chargen/portal/api/auth-hardening, 182 tests) green.

### 2026-06-16 — T3.21 security tail: public aiohttp surface hardening (headers + request-size cap) — *drop t321-web-security-headers*
T3.21 MEDIUM tail (Opus lane) — the browser-facing aiohttp app (`server/web_client.py`) serves the SPA (which renders server-provided strings) and the chargen/portal JSON API to unauthenticated clients, but shipped with **zero security response headers** and aiohttp's default 1 MiB request-body limit. Closes the "aiohttp surface (CORS, headers, request-size/DoS limits)" + "web-client XSS/injection surface" scope items. No schema change; no behavior change for legitimate clients.
- **App-wide security-headers middleware** (`_security_headers_middleware`): applies `X-Content-Type-Options: nosniff` (stop MIME-sniffing of API JSON as HTML), `X-Frame-Options: DENY` + CSP `frame-ancestors 'none'` (clickjacking, belt-and-suspenders across legacy + modern browsers), CSP `base-uri 'self'` / `object-src 'none'` (block `<base>`-tag hijack + plugin/object embeds), `Referrer-Policy: strict-origin-when-cross-origin`, and `Permissions-Policy: geolocation=(), microphone=(), camera=()`. Uses `setdefault` (a handler's own header always wins), applies to **raised** HTTPExceptions too (404/413/429/500 carry the protections), and **skips already-prepared WebSocket** upgrades.
- **CSP is deliberately MINIMAL** — the SPA relies on inline `<script>`, inline `onclick=`, and 96 inline `style=` attributes, so a `script-src`/`default-src` directive would break the client. Only the frame/base/object vectors the SPA never uses are restricted. A test pins this so a future well-meaning tightening can't silently brick the client. **HSTS intentionally omitted** (an HTTPS/deployment decision for the operator's TLS proxy, not this plain-HTTP origin).
- **Explicit request-size cap**: `web.Application(client_max_size=_MAX_REQUEST_BYTES, …)` — default **256 KiB** (all client bodies are small JSON; chargen/login are single-digit KB → 30×+ headroom), tighter than aiohttp's 1 MiB default so a hostile client can't stream a multi-megabyte body to amplify memory pressure on the single shared DB worker. Operator-overridable (raise OR lower) via `SWMUSH_MAX_REQUEST_BYTES`; garbage / non-positive falls back to the default.
- **14 tests green** (`tests/test_t321_security_headers.py` — header set, minimal-CSP guard, HSTS-absent guard, middleware on normal/error/clobber/prepared-WS responses, env-override + garbage-fallback for the size cap, live-Application wiring, import-clean). Verified against `test_portal_login_throttle` + `test_api_auth_hardening` + hygiene + smoke (47 passed / 1 skipped, single-process).

### 2026-06-16 — T3.21 HIGH: sanitize Director LLM headlines before player display — *drop t321-news-sanitize* (Opus lane)
Closes the last T3.21 HIGH finding (Director output not sanitized before display). The Director's faction-turn `news_headline` is LLM-generated and reaches players verbatim via the `news` command (telnet) and `/api/portal/news` (web). A poisoned/erratic headline carrying ANSI/VT or control bytes could rewrite a telnet terminal (cursor moves, screen clears, colour spoofing) or smuggle control characters into the web feed.
- **`server/ansi.py` (new helper):** `sanitize_for_display(text, max_len=200)` strips CSI/OSC/bare-ESC escape sequences and C0/C1 control chars (incl. DEL), collapses whitespace to a single line, and caps length. Precompiled patterns; dependency-free (only `re`).
- **Applied at the display seams (not the avoid-lane producer):** `server/web_portal.py` `handle_news` and `parser/news_commands.py` `NewsCommand.execute` now route the stored `summary` through it before it reaches a client. Output-side sanitization keeps the fix entirely out of `engine/director.py` (avoid-lane) **and** also cleans any rows stored before this guard existed. The web SPA already HTML-escapes on render (`esc()`/`escapeHtml()`), so this is server-side defence in depth there; for telnet it closes a genuine terminal-injection gap.
- **No schema change.** `tests/test_t321_news_sanitize.py` (12: CSI/OSC/bare-ESC/control-char/C1/CR-overwrite stripping, unicode + plain-text preservation, whitespace collapse, length cap, empty/None guard, + AST checks that both seams actually call the sanitizer).

### 2026-06-16 — T3.21 optimization: index the account → characters lookup (schema v46) — *drop t321-characters-account-index*
Performance drop. Pure index addition; query results byte-for-byte identical, no behavior change.
- **`db/database.py` schema v46.** The account → characters lookup had no supporting index. `Database.get_characters(account_id)` — run on every login and character-selection — did `SELECT * FROM characters WHERE account_id = ? AND is_active = 1`, a full `characters` scan that grows with every character in the game; the accounts↔characters JOINs in builder/mux tooling (`parser/building_tier2`, `parser/mux_commands`) join on `c.account_id`, also unindexed. Adds composite `CREATE INDEX idx_characters_account ON characters(account_id, is_active)` to BOTH the base `SCHEMA_SQL` (fresh DBs) and `MIGRATIONS[46]` (existing DBs, `IF NOT EXISTS` → idempotent). The composite fully covers the get_characters predicate (account_id + is_active) and serves the `account_id`-prefix JOINs.
- **Verified:** `EXPLAIN QUERY PLAN` for the get_characters query now reports `SEARCH ... USING INDEX idx_characters_account` (no more `SCAN characters`).
- **Files:** `db/database.py` (SCHEMA_VERSION 45→46, base-schema index, MIGRATIONS[46]), `tests/test_t321_characters_account_index.py` (new, 6 tests: schema-version floor, index present on fresh DB, migration recreates index, migration idempotent, query-plan uses index, get_characters results unchanged), `tests/test_t321_admin_audit.py` (de-pinned the brittle exact `SCHEMA_VERSION == 45` assertion → assert admin_audit landed at migration key 45 and version ≥ 45), `CHANGELOG.md`, `TODO.json`.

### 2026-06-16 — T3.21 optimization: kill the N+1 in the character directory — *drop t321-portal-characters-n1*
Performance drop on a PUBLIC, unauthenticated endpoint. No schema change, behavior-preserving.
- **`server/web_portal.py` `handle_characters` (GET /api/portal/characters).** The paginated directory fetched the page of rows, then looped and called `db.get_character(row["id"])` ONCE PER ROW solely to read the `faction` field out of the attributes JSON blob — up to `per_page` (capped 50) extra full-character DB round-trips per page request, on an open endpoint = a real load / DoS-amplification vector. The page query now SELECTs the `attributes` column inline and faction is parsed from that row, so a directory page costs exactly two queries (count + page) regardless of page size. Faction values, the faction filter, and the response shape are all unchanged; malformed/missing attributes still degrade to `"Neutral"` without crashing.
- **Files:** `server/web_portal.py`, `tests/test_portal_characters_n1.py` (new, 6 tests: inline-faction parse, zero per-row get_character calls, malformed/missing-blob → Neutral, faction filter against the inline value, page SELECT carries attributes, response-shape preserved), `CHANGELOG.md`, `TODO.json`.

### 2026-06-16 — T3.21 HIGH: api.py auth-surface hardening (token-secret persistence + XFF spoof-resistance) — *drop t321-api-auth-hardening*
Security drop closing the two HIGH-severity findings from the T3.21 audit that both live on the `server/api.py` auth/rate-limit surface. No schema change. Default behavior is unchanged for the current single-box deployment; both fixes are inert until configured / first token use.
- **Login-token secret now persists (`server/api.py`).** The HMAC secret was `os.urandom(32)` at import, so every server restart silently invalidated every outstanding login token (mass re-auth). It is now loaded-or-created from a gitignored 0600 key file (`token_secret.key`, overridable via `SWMUSH_TOKEN_SECRET_FILE`), lazily on first token use so merely importing the module never creates a file. On any IO/permission failure it degrades safely to an ephemeral in-process secret (the prior behavior) rather than failing closed.
  - **Windows correctness fix folded in:** `os.open` defaults to *text* mode on Windows, which would translate any `0x0A` byte in the random secret to `0x0D0A` on write and corrupt the persisted secret — so after a restart the reloaded secret would mismatch and invalidate all tokens, defeating the fix on the production (Windows) box. Now opens with `O_BINARY` (0 on POSIX).
- **X-Forwarded-For is no longer trusted blindly (`server/api.py` `_get_client_ip`).** It honored the leading XFF entry unconditionally, letting a raw-socket client spoof its source IP and defeat the per-IP rate limiters (chargen create + portal login throttle, which both key on this helper). XFF is now honored ONLY when the direct peer is an operator-configured trusted proxy (`SWMUSH_TRUSTED_PROXIES`, comma-separated allowlist), returning the right-most non-proxy hop (append-resistant for proxy chains). Default (no proxies configured) = direct connection = peername only = un-spoofable. Updated the now-stale spoofability note in `server/web_portal.py`.
- **Files:** `server/api.py`, `server/web_portal.py` (comment), `.gitignore` (`token_secret.key`), `tests/test_api_auth_hardening.py` (new, 17 tests: persistence/restart-stability/binary-mode/atomic-write-no-clobber/fallback + the full XFF trust matrix incl. all-trusted-chain + None-transport), `CHANGELOG.md`, `TODO.json`.
- **Hardened per code-review (folded in pre-merge):** (a) atomic temp-then-`os.replace` for the secret write so a failed/partial write never truncates an existing valid key file (which would loop token invalidation across restarts); (b) the all-trusted-XFF-chain edge now falls back to the un-spoofable direct peer instead of the leading XFF entry; (c) `_get_client_ip` guards `request.transport is None`.

### 2026-06-15 — T3.21 Blocker 3: admin authority re-validation + admin_audit trail (schema v45) — *drop t321-admin-audit*
Closes the third (fork-free) T3.21 launch-blocker (`docs/design/HANDOFF_t3_21_security_optimization_2026-06-13.md`), re-audited against HEAD. Two related admin-authority gaps:
- **Never-revalidated admin snapshot (`parser/commands.py` `check_access`).** The BUILDER/ADMIN tiers read `is_admin`/`is_builder` from `session.account` — a snapshot frozen at **login**. A privilege revoked mid-session kept working until the player disconnected. Fixed: `check_access` now re-reads the flag from the DB on **every** elevated dispatch via the new `Database.get_account_privileges(account_id) -> (is_admin, is_builder)`, and syncs **both** flags on the in-memory snapshot to match (one round-trip already fetched both, so other code reading `session.account` also sees the revocation). PLAYER/ANYONE tiers are untouched and incur **no** DB hit — only the rare elevated commands pay one indexed PK lookup. Falls back to the snapshot only when no DB handle is present or on a transient DB error (no worse than the pre-fix behavior).
- **No audit trail.** There was no record of who exercised privilege. Added an append-only **`admin_audit`** table (schema **v45**; in both `SCHEMA_SQL` and `MIGRATIONS[45]`, with `idx_admin_audit_account`/`idx_admin_audit_created`) written at the parser dispatch seam (`_execute`) for **every** BUILDER/ADMIN command that passes the access gate, via `Database.record_admin_action(...)`. Captures account/username/char/access_level/command/detail/timestamp.
- **Secret redaction.** `detail` is sanitized by `_redact_audit_detail` before insert: `@newpassword`/`@passwd`/`@password`/`@newpass` are redacted wholesale, AND any arg string containing `passwd`/`password` OR any whitespace token that is itself a redact-set command (both catch a reset smuggled through `@force`, even an alias lacking the literal `password` substring) is redacted — so a plaintext password reset can **never** land in the audit log. Ordinary args are capped at 500 chars. The audit write is best-effort (`_audit_privileged` swallows all errors) so an audit failure never blocks the operator's command.
- **Verified:** new `tests/test_t321_admin_audit.py` (19 — schema v45 + table/index shape, `get_account_privileges` live read + revocation, `record_admin_action` insert, `check_access` denies a revoked admin despite a stale snapshot + syncs it + builder-flag + no-account + no-DB-fallback + PLAYER/ANYONE unchanged, redaction matrix, end-to-end seam write with `@newpassword` redacted, audit-never-raises) + existing `test_secmod1_admin_security` / `test_cities_phase6_admin` / `test_wow2a` admin suites + db-integrity + hygiene + boot smoke (195 green single-process). Era-clean, no funnel touched, additive schema.
- **Files:** `db/database.py` (SCHEMA_VERSION 44→45, `admin_audit` table + indexes in SCHEMA_SQL + MIGRATIONS[45], `get_account_privileges`, `record_admin_action`), `parser/commands.py` (`check_access` re-validation + `_live_account_flag`, `_audit_privileged` + `_redact_audit_detail` at the dispatch seam), `tests/test_t321_admin_audit.py` (new), `CHANGELOG.md`, `TODO.json`.

### 2026-06-15 — T3.21 security pre-pass (fork-free slice): portal login throttle + swallowed faction-membership bug — *drop t321-login-throttle*
First slice of the T3.21 security pre-pass (`docs/design/HANDOFF_t3_21_security_optimization_2026-06-13.md`), re-audited against HEAD (the handoff is a 2026-06-13 timeslice). Ships the two **fork-free** blocker fixes; the third blocker's IDOR sub-question turned out to be a design fork and is logged for Brian (see below).
- **Per-IP portal login throttle (Blocker 2).** `server/web_portal.py` `handle_login` had **no rate limit** — it went straight to `db.authenticate`, and the only throttle (`authenticate`'s 5-fail/5-min) is **per-account**, so credential-stuffing *across* many accounts from one IP was unbounded. Added a dedicated `_login_rate_ok(ip)` bucket (10 login POSTs / 60s / IP; reuses `server.api._get_client_ip`) returning **429** before authenticate. Dedicated bucket (not the shared `api._check_rate_limit`) so login throttling is independent of the general API budget. (Keyed on `_get_client_ip`, which honors `X-Forwarded-For` — correct behind a trusted proxy, spoofable on a raw socket; the XFF-hardening item stays tracked separately.)
- **Swallowed faction-membership bug.** `handle_character`'s membership query used `WHERE m.character_id` on `org_memberships`, which is keyed by **`char_id`** — the wrong column raised "no such column", was swallowed by the bare `except`, and `faction_membership` was **silently never populated** on any profile. Fixed to `m.char_id`.
- **Design fork LOGGED, not guessed (Blocker 1 / IDOR).** The audit called `handle_character` returning `online`/`achievement_count`/`scene_count` for any char_id an unauthenticated "who's-online map". Re-audit caught the missing context: the character **directory** (`handle_characters`) is *also* fully public and already returns `online` for every character **by design** — so whether player online/activity status is public (social) or private (anti-stalking) is a **product decision**, not a bug. Logged as `SEC.player_online_activity_visibility` in `design_calls_pending_brian` (recommend B: auth-gate both directory + profile). Blocker 3 (admin re-validation + audit table) is fork-free and queued next.
- **Verified:** new `tests/test_portal_login_throttle.py` (4 — throttle blocks after max, per-IP isolation, handle_login wires it + 429, faction query uses the correct column) + portal smoke + boot smoke (17 green single-process).
- **Files:** `server/web_portal.py`, `tests/test_portal_login_throttle.py` (new), `CHANGELOG.md`, `TODO.json`.

### 2026-06-15 — T3.19 Phase 1: externalize the HIGH-priority economy knobs — *drop t319-phase1-econ-knobs*
Builds on Phase 0's `engine/tunables.py` foundation. Externalizes the 8 highest-leverage economy balance values into `data/tunables.yaml` so they can be tuned post-launch without a code change. **Every knob is read at its USE SITE** via `get_tunable("<key>", <in-code default>)` — never at module import — because `load_tunables()` runs at boot (`game_server.py:607`) *after* the engine modules import, so a module-level read would freeze to the default (a silent phantom externalization). Each YAML value equals the in-code default, so the change is **behavior-identical** to the pre-drop state (empty/missing YAML → same values).
- **`trade.price_source_multiplier` (0.70) / `trade.price_demand_multiplier` (1.40)** — `engine/trading.py` `get_planet_price`.
- **`trade.supply_refresh_seconds` (2700)** — `engine/trading.py` `SupplyPool._refreshed` + `seconds_until_refresh`.
- **`trade.supply_max_luxury_goods` (6)** — `engine/trading.py` `_max_units` (luxury_goods only; other goods untouched).
- **`mission.reward_smuggling_max` (5000)** — `engine/missions.py` `_scale_reward` (SMUGGLING band top; other types untouched).
- **`bounty.reward_superior_max` (10000)** — `engine/bounty_board.py` `_scale_reward` (SUPERIOR tier top; other tiers untouched).
- **`p2p.tax_pct` (5)** — `parser/builtin_commands.py` credit-trade tax. Re-expressed `max(1, amount // 20)` as `max(1, amount * tax_pct // 100)`; with `pct=5` this is **integer-identical** to the old `amount // 20` for all amounts (verified by sweep — no float drift), so the 5% p2p sink is byte-for-byte preserved.
- **`commissary.sellback_rate` (0.50)** — `engine/commissary.py` `_refund_amount`.
- **Operator-misconfig hardening (from an adversarial verification pass):** (a) `get_tunable` now coerces a **present-but-null** YAML value (`key:` with no value → `None`) to the in-code default — `dict.get` only defaults on an *absent* key, so a valueless-key typo would otherwise feed `None` into call-site arithmetic and crash 4/5 sites; falsy-but-valid values (`0`/`False`) are preserved. (b) `bounty.reward_superior_max` is clamped `>= lo` so an out-of-range value can't make `random.randint` raise "empty range".
- **Verified:** new `tests/test_t3_19_phase1_econ_knobs.py` (16 — default-then-override for each knob, band-collapse determinism for the RNG rewards, cross-type/tier non-interference, p2p integer-identity, null-coercion + null-no-crash + bounty out-of-range-no-crash, YAML ships cluster) + Phase-0 `test_t3_19_tunables_foundation.py` updated for the now-populated YAML + trading/missions/bounty/commissary regression + boot smoke (green). 4-lens adversarial verification (behavior-preservation / invariants / correctness / boot) all clean after the hardening. Behavior-preserving; no funnel/era/schema change.

### 2026-06-15 — T3.19 Phase 0: tunables foundation — *drop t3-19-phase0*
T3.19 Phase 0: infrastructure only — no knob is externalized yet. Establishes the runtime machinery and the empty-YAML boot path.
- **`engine/tunables.py` (new):** `load_tunables(path)` reads a flat-namespace YAML (`trade.price_demand_multiplier: 1.40`, etc.) into a module-level dict; `get_tunable(key, default)` returns the loaded value or the caller's in-code default (absent key = byte-identical to today's hardcoded literal); `reset_tunables()` for test isolation. Missing file → INFO log + no-op; malformed YAML or non-mapping top-level → ERROR log + no-op. Mirrors `engine/director_config_loader.py` (YAML-overrides-with-in-code-default, fail-open). Call sites: `from engine.tunables import get_tunable` — placed in engine/, not server/, to avoid circular imports from engine code.
- **`data/tunables.yaml` (new):** empty dict `{}` with header comment describing the Phase 1 economy knob names. A missing or empty file is always safe — every call site supplies the current hardcoded value as `default`.
- **`server/game_server.py`:** added `load_tunables("data/tunables.yaml")` call early in `GameServer.start()` (after DB init, before market pool hydration), wrapped in try/except fail-open.
- **Verified:** `tests/test_t3_19_tunables_foundation.py` (13 new — empty YAML, None YAML, missing file, valid round-trip x3 types, bad YAML, non-mapping, reload replaces previous, default-path file exists + Phase-0 empty, key-absent returns None/custom-default, type preservation float/int, hardcoded-default-passthrough, boot wiring) + hygiene + smoke = 29 green single-process.
- **Files:** `engine/tunables.py` (new), `data/tunables.yaml` (new), `server/game_server.py`, `tests/test_t3_19_tunables_foundation.py` (new), `CHANGELOG.md`, `TODO.json`.

### 2026-06-15 — Contest: stop orphaning Anchor NPCs on resolution + harden the state machine — *drop contest-anchor-reland*
Fix drop off the engine defect-hunt backlog (`docs/design/HANDOFF_engine_defect_hunt_2026-06-14.md`), re-landed onto current `main` (the fix was committed on the stale `drop/t3-20-safe-load` lane and never integrated; `engine/contest.py` is byte-identical between that lane's base and `main`, so the re-land is clean). Four confirmed defects in `engine/contest.py`, all in the Region-Anchor lifecycle / resolution state machine:
- **Anchor NPCs never despawned on resolution (HIGH).** When a region contest resolved by ANY path, the Region Anchor NPC and its 0–4 reinforcements were **never deleted** — they're created via `db.create_npc` and never registered in `region_garrison`, so `dismiss_region_garrison` (which only deletes garrison-table rows) could never reach them, and no reaper tick exists. The common outcome (defender-win-by-default at `ends_at`) left a hostile, HP-buffed, aggressive Anchor + reinforcements **alive in the landmark room forever**, attacking players who entered after the contest ended. **Fix:** a new `_despawn_contest_anchor(db, contest)` deletes the pinned `anchor_npc_id` (via `db.delete_npc`) + every reinforcement (`DELETE FROM npcs WHERE json_extract(ai_config_json,'$.anchor_reinforcement_for')=<id>`), called from **both** `_resolve_defender_win` and `_resolve_challenger_win` — which between them cover every resolution path (`on_npc_killed_in_combat` delegates to them). Best-effort: a delete failure logs but never blocks resolution.
- **Resolution UPDATE had no compare-and-swap (LOW).** Both resolution functions did `UPDATE … SET status=… WHERE id=?` with no `AND status='active'` guard and no rowcount check, so at the `ends_at` boundary a killing-blow challenger-win and the tick-expiry defender-win could both fire and double-apply a penalty/cooldown. **Fix:** `… WHERE id=? AND status='active'` + bail when `rowcount==0` (the loser of the race becomes a clean no-op — and does not double-despawn).
- **Anchor spawn not idempotent on pin failure (MEDIUM).** If the `anchor_npc_id` pin UPDATE failed after the NPC was created, the orphan stayed live + unpinned and the next tick (still `anchor_npc_id IS NULL`) spawned a **second** Anchor. **Fix:** early-return if the contest is already pinned; on pin failure, delete the just-created orphan and bail so the next tick re-spawns cleanly.
- **Stale-anchor reuse via name de-dup (MEDIUM).** The deterministic `"<prefix> of <region>"` name + `create_npc`'s `(name,room_id)` de-dup handed back a *leftover* Anchor on a later same-landmark contest. **Fix:** per-contest-unique name `"… (#<contest_id>)"` (belt-and-suspenders with despawn-on-resolution).
- **Verified:** new `tests/test_contest_anchor_lifecycle.py` (9 — despawn deletes anchor+reinforcements; both resolution paths despawn; the CAS no-op skips despawn/penalty; spawn early-returns when already pinned; + source guards on the unique name and pin-failure cleanup) + contest/territory regression green. Engine-only; `db.delete_npc` is an existing method (no contested file touched).
- **Files:** `engine/contest.py`, `tests/test_contest_anchor_lifecycle.py` (new), `CHANGELOG.md`, `TODO.json`.

Windu deployed'` → `'Static · Jedi Vanguard deployed'`. Era-clean; Q1 compliant.

### 2026-06-15 — Durable loop → flat-rate subscription auth (was metered API, $0-balance) — *drop loop-subscription-auth*
Tooling fix (the autonomous-loop economics + the reason it produced nothing all day). The headless `claude -p` launcher inherited the user-scope `ANTHROPIC_API_KEY`, which (a) billed **pay-per-token Opus (~$31/day)** and (b) had a **$0 prepaid balance** → every hourly fire died "Credit balance is too low" (13 no-op fires 06-15). Fix: `build_launcher` now emits `set "ANTHROPIC_API_KEY="` after `setlocal`, so headless `claude -p` falls back to the logged-in **Claude Max subscription** (verified working headless on this box) — **flat rate, no per-token fees.** Combined with arming `--model sonnet` (the loop's work is mechanical; Opus reserved for interactive judgment), the all-day loop becomes economically viable.
- **Files:** `tools/durable_loop.py`, `CHANGELOG.md`. (Tooling only — no game-code/schema change.)

### 2026-06-15 — T3.16 Space Wildspace Drop 2b: faction caches + rep-funnel resolution — *drop t316-wildspace-faction-caches*
Resolves the Drop 1a `zone_id=0` rep blocker and ships the rep-bearing `faction_cache` layer on the Sieges Theater. Per `docs/design/space_wildspace_design_v1.md` §4.3 / §4.4 / §8 Drop 2.
- **Rep funnel resolved (`engine/space_caches.py`):** cache rep rewards now route through `engine.organizations.adjust_rep` (personal faction standing — the *same* rep the cache-visibility gate reads via `get_all_faction_reps`/`is_cache_visible`), via a shared `_apply_rep_rewards` helper. The Drop 1a placeholder wrote rewards through `adjust_territory_influence(..., zone_id=0, ...)`, but wildspace zones have no territory row, so the reward landed on a phantom zone 0 that no display reads. `adjust_rep` is the correct funnel (territory influence is per-zone org *control*, a different concept) and makes the reward real (rep tier, shop discounts, cache visibility). Both `harvest_mining` and the new faction-cache path use it.
- **`harvest_faction_cache` (`engine/space_caches.py`):** new harvest path for `kind: faction_cache` — **no skill check** (a marker, not a challenge, §4.3); rolls the yield table, grants resources via `engine.crafting.add_resource`, applies rep via the funnel, sets cooldown. Yields resources + rep only — **no credits** (keeps the wildspace loop off the credit faucet/sink ledger). Symmetric `wrong_kind` guards: `mine` on a faction cache and `harvest` on a mining node both refuse and redirect.
- **Density-inflation fix (`spawn_zone_caches`):** now counts **non-depleted** (`available` + `cooldown`) instances against `density`, not just `available`. The Drop 1a count-available-only behaviour over-spawned — each harvest sent a node to cooldown, the next spawn topped `available` back to density, and when the cooled node flipped back the zone grew to `density+N` nodes unboundedly across play. Counting non-depleted keeps `density` = max concurrent nodes and lets `respawn_minutes` actually gate re-availability. Fresh-spawn behaviour is unchanged (existing Drop-1a spawn tests still pass).
- **`parser/space_commands.py` + `parser/harvest_command.py`:** the space faction-cache harvest routes through the **existing `harvest` verb** (extend, don't add) — `handle_space_harvest(ctx)` is early-dispatched from the ground `HarvestCommand`: aboard a ship in open space, `harvest` lists/recovers wildspace faction caches; otherwise it falls through to ground wilderness harvest (try/except-guarded with ground fallback). No colliding second command registration. `mine`'s listing is now filtered to mining nodes only (faction caches show under `harvest`).
- **`data/worlds/clone_wars/wildspace/sieges.yaml`:** 6 faction caches added (additive) — `geonosis_front`: clone survival pods (`republic` +2), Jedi recovery beacons (`jedi_order` +5; the sole player-reachable `kyber_shard_minor` faucet — density 1, 180-min respawn), CIS recovery markers (`cis` +2), clone-bounty dead drops (`bounty_hunters_guild` +2); `outer_rim_sieges_drift`: lost Jedi artifact beacons (`jedi_order` +4), Hutt salvage claims (`hutt_cartel` +3). All faction-gated (never universal), rep deltas 2–5 per §4.4.
- **`tests/test_space_faction_cache.py` (NEW, 11):** rep-funnel proof (calls `adjust_rep`, never `adjust_territory_influence`; rep lands on a seeded org); harvest happy-path (no skill check, resource + cooldown); wrong-kind both directions; not-found / cooldown guards; spawn no-inflation (cooldown counts, depleted refills); `harvest`-verb space dispatch (declines when not aboard, takes it when aboard). **`tests/test_space_caches_sieges.py`:** the Drop-2 mining-only/no-rep invariant split into mining-rep-free + faction-caches-rep-bearing-with-valid-codes; added Jedi/BHG visibility-gating tests.
- **Verified:** 57 green (11 new + Drop-1a 26 + sieges 20) + hygiene + smoke-foundation, single-process. Era-clean. No schema change (reuses the `space_caches` table + states).

### 2026-06-15 — T3.16 Space Wildspace Drop 2: Sieges Theater (mining player-reachable + faction visibility) — *drop t316-wildspace-sieges*
Makes the Drop 1a cache loop reachable in-game. Drop 1a (`d653e1a`) shipped the engine (`engine/space_caches.py`) + the `mine` command, but only wired a dev-only zone (`DEV_TEST_ZONE_KEY`), so no player could mine. This drop adds the two **Sieges Theater** wildspace zones to the live CW zone graph with real cache pools, so `mine` works in space. Faction-cache **visibility** is now live (republic/cis-gated nodes); faction-cache **rep rewards** stay deferred (see below). Per `docs/design/space_wildspace_design_v1.md` §3.1 / §4 / §8 Drop 2.

(The §6.4 Director/traffic knobs — `friendly_traffic_density` etc. — are deliberately **not** added: their only consumers are in the Director lane, so adding them now would be phantom fields.)

Both `deep_space` type → `get_space_security()` returns `lawless` (open PvP) by the type default, satisfying the design's LAWLESS requirement with **no security override** (space PvP is not governed by `engine/security.py`, which is room-based). DEV pool unchanged. Adding Hutt Frontier (Drop 3) is a one-line table entry.

### 2026-06-15 — XSS hardening: remove dead `ev.html` fast-path + escape regression tests — *drop xss-harden-ev-html*
Closes audit Section B **DEV-5/UX-8** (`docs/design/06_Claude_Response_and_Action_Items.md`). The web client's event renderer carried an `ev.html || ansiToHtml(ev.text)` fast-path in 13 places: any event with an `html` field would have been injected into `innerHTML` **unescaped**. Verified at HEAD that `ev.html` has **zero producers** (no `"html"` dict key anywhere in `server/`/`engine/`/`parser/`; no `html:` event construction in `static/`), so the branch was pure latent footgun. Removing it makes the `ansiToHtml(ev.text)` → `escapeHtml` escape path mandatory for all user-reachable text. Client-only + tests; no engine/schema change.
- **`static/client.html`:** dropped the `ev.html ||` fallback from all 13 render sites (`buildRow` desc/pose/comm-in/sys-*/ooc/plain + `buildCommsRow` comm/ooc/sys); updated the event-shape doc comment to record that there is deliberately **no** `html` field.
- **`tests/test_xss_hardening_invariant.py` (NEW, 4):** producer-side invariant (no `html` event-dict key in server/engine/parser) + consumer guards (`buildRow`/`buildCommsRow` carry no `ev.html`; user text routed through `ansiToHtml`→`escapeHtml`). Pure-python, runs in the default suite.
- **`tests/spa/test_xss_event_escaping.py` (NEW, 5):** runtime proof — extracts `escapeHtml`/`ansiToHtml` from `client.html` and evals them in bare Node (no jsdom): `<script>`/`<img onerror>`/`"><svg onload>` payloads all render escaped; the legitimate ANSI→color-span path still works. Skips cleanly if Node absent.
- **Verified:** 9 new tests green (Node present → escape proof ran, not skipped) + hygiene(2) + smoke-foundation. Era-clean. Single-process gate.

### 2026-06-15 — T3.16 Space Wildspace Drop 1a: cache framework + mining loop — *drop t316-wildspace-drop1a*
First slice of T3.16 (Space Wildspace, per `space_wildspace_design_v1.md` §4/§8). Builds the **resource-cache framework + the `mine` loop** end-to-end in a dev test zone. ### 2026-06-14 — T3.13 Padawan/Master: +authorize Master pre-authorization (P5, OPT C) — *drop pm-authorize*
Builds the resolved design fork `PM.approval_pending_store` = **OPTION C** (pre-authorization-only at launch). Closes the T3.13 P5 approval-weight gap (design §5.3) **without** the cross-cutting per-action `+approve`/`+deny` block-and-wait interception layer (deferred post-launch). Parser-only; no engine/schema change.
- **`+authorize <padawan> <category> [off]`** (`parser/padawan_master_trials.py`, new `AuthorizeCommand`, alias `authorise`): a Master grants/revokes a **standing** pre-authorization for a category of otherwise approval-gated action. Three categories map to the §5.3 gated actions — `offworld` (leave Coruscant for non-sanctioned missions), `powers` (use Force powers in the field), `trials` (attempt the Trials without a fresh `+endorse`). Forms: `<padawan> <category>`, sole-bond shorthand `<category>`, list `<padawan>`, and a bare context list (Padawan sees their own clearances; Master sees their sole Padawan's). Master-or-staff gated; both sides notified + bilateral audit log (`pm_authorization`).
- **Storage mirrors `+endorse`:** a `master_authorizations` JSON list on the Padawan's `chargen_notes` (no schema migration, per-Padawan, `..._by_id` audit). Category aliases (`force`→`powers`, `travel`/`mission`→`offworld`, `trial`→`trials`) normalize; unknown categories rejected.
- **Real consumer (no phantom):** the `+trials` display now renders an **Endorsement** line — `standing` when the `trials` category is pre-authorized (the persistent complement to the one-shot `+endorse`), `ready` when a one-shot endorsement is held, else `none` (must `+endorse`/`+authorize`). The `+authorize` list views consume the `offworld`/`powers` grants; the §5.3 mechanical action-gates read these standing grants when/where built (OPT C: the gated actions just check the pre-authorization).
- **Verified:** new `tests/test_pm_authorize.py` (16 — grant/alias/idempotent, sole-bond shorthand, revoke + no-op, bad-category/no-bond/not-the-master guards, master+padawan list views, padawan notify, the 3 `+trials` endorsement states, registration) + full PM suite (`test_pm1/2/3*`, `test_pm_leave_master`) = 165 green.
- **Files:** `parser/padawan_master_trials.py`, `tests/test_pm_authorize.py` (new), `CHANGELOG.md`, `TODO.json`.

### 2026-06-14 — Web a11y: prefers-reduced-motion + modal return-focus (audit UX-6) — *drop a11y-reduced-motion-focus*
Picks up the unclaimed accessibility item from the ChatGPT-audit response (`docs/design/06_Claude_Response_and_Action_Items.md`, Section B / UX-6). Client-only, purely additive (+42 lines, 0 removed) to `static/client.html`.
- **`prefers-reduced-motion`:** a `@media (prefers-reduced-motion: reduce)` block neutralizes animation/transition duration + iteration globally (the standard near-zero pattern, not hard `none`, to avoid `transitionend`/`animationend` timing bugs) — respects the OS/browser reduced-motion preference for vestibular-sensitive players. Only active when requested.
- **Modal return-focus:** `_a11yRememberOpener()` / `_a11yRestoreFocus()` capture `document.activeElement` on modal open and restore it on close, wired into all 5 `role="dialog"` modals (sheet-panel, inv/shop/board/craft); the existing Escape→close handlers inherit it. (Full Tab focus-trap deferred — it needs runtime verification; map/region/city panels aren't `role="dialog"` so out of scope.)
- **Verified:** new `tests/spa/test_a11y_reduced_motion_focus.py` (22) + onclick-exports regression (4) green. No existing behavior altered.
- **Files:** `static/client.html`, `tests/spa/test_a11y_reduced_motion_focus.py` (new), `CHANGELOG.md`, `TODO.json`.

### 2026-06-14 — Kyber attunement → weekly-ceremonial (Brian roadmap decision 3) — *drop kyber-weekly-ceremonial*
Executes `BRIAN_ROADMAP_DECISIONS.2026-06-14` #3 (resolves `TUN.kyber.cooldown` / `.quality_band` / `.skill_difficulty`): kyber is **ceremonial-for-Jedi, not a common harvest.** Engine-only tuning in `engine/kyber_attunement.py`; no schema/funnel change.
- **Difficulty 11 → 15** (`ATTUNE_DIFFICULTY`): Moderate → Difficult — a Padawan no longer auto-passes.
- **Cooldown 24h → 7d + per-CHARACTER global** (`ATTUNE_COOLDOWN_SECS = 7*24*60*60`; `cd_key` changed from per-landmark `attune_{room_id}` to the character-global `attune_weekly`): **one kyber draw per Jedi per week across ALL resonant sites** — closes the prior 4-shards/day farm (4 landmarks × 24h) by making the cooldown character-scoped, not site-scoped.
- **Quality floor 75 → 65** (`QUALITY_FLOOR`): a marginal attune now yields a **sub-q75 "dud"** below the `T5_MIN_QUALITY=75` lightsaber gate. With the +5Q/5-margin band, a **+10 skill margin** reaches q75 (usable) and +30 caps q95 — reverses the prior "no duds, every success is lightsaber-grade" design. The success message now flags dud-vs-true ("its core is clouded… a lesser focus" / "it rings true… anchor a blade"); the cooldown/fail flavor updated to weekly.
- **Verified:** `tests/test_syn6c_t5_crafting_and_harvest_nodes.py` updated to the new band (margin 0 → q65 dud, +10 → q75) + new tests for the dud-vs-T5-gate and the **global cooldown blocking a *different* landmark**; 43 passed. - **Files:** `engine/kyber_attunement.py`, `tests/test_syn6c_t5_crafting_and_harvest_nodes.py`, `docs/design/economy_tuning_open_questions_v1.md`, `CHANGELOG.md`, `TODO.json`.

### 2026-06-14 — Fix the `@newpassword` bcrypt defect + login fail-closed + dead move-alias (audit-confirmed bugs) — *drop audit-confirmed-fixes*
Fixes the confirmed code defects from the 2026-06-14 external (ChatGPT) audit, each verified at symbol level against HEAD (full response in `docs/design/06_Claude_Response_and_Action_Items.md`; the audit set is `docs/design/00`–`05`).
- **P0 — `@newpassword` wrote an unreadable hash.** `parser/mux_commands.py::NewPasswordCommand` hashed the new password with raw `hashlib.sha256(...).hexdigest()` and wrote the 64-char hex into `accounts.password_hash`, but `db/database.py::authenticate` verifies with `bcrypt.checkpw`. `checkpw` **raises** `ValueError("Invalid salt")` on a non-bcrypt string (confirmed empirically — it does not return `False`), so **every account an admin reset became permanently un-loginable** (Telnet `connect` had no guard there → the exception killed the login coroutine; the web portal caught it → HTTP 500). Fix: hash with `bcrypt.hashpw(new_pass.encode("utf-8"), bcrypt.gensalt()).decode("utf-8")` — the same scheme `create_account` uses. This was a real, shipped, **untracked** defect with no in-game recovery path.
- **Password-length parity.** The reset path hard-coded a weaker `< 4` floor while account/char creation enforces `server.config.Config.min_password_len` (6). Reset now uses `< 6` to share one floor.
- **Login fail-closed hardening.** `authenticate` now wraps `bcrypt.checkpw` in `try/except (ValueError, TypeError)` → treats a malformed/legacy stored hash as a bad password instead of letting the exception escape the login path. This **rescues accounts already bricked** by the old bug (they fail login cleanly and can be re-reset with the now-correct command).
- **Dead `move`→`repair` alias removed.** `parser/builtin_commands.py::MoveCommand` carried a stray `aliases=["repair"]` (a movement verb owning `repair` is a copy-paste slip). Runtime effect was nil (ship DamCon owns `repair` via last-writer-wins registration), but it's removed so it can't shadow a real `repair` handler in any registry built without space commands.
- **Doc hygiene — closed a stale OBS.** `TODO.json::OBS.quality_and_boosts_not_combat_read` still read `OPEN — design pass candidate` ("experiment boosts may be display-only") even though crafted quality→combat shipped in Drops 19/44/45 (weapons/armor/consumables, hard-capped, read in combat). That stale entry **seeded the audit's incorrect "#1 P1 launch blocker."** Flipped to RESOLVED with pointers to the shipped code + the ratified design call.
- **Deferred by design (NOT in this drop):** the command-registry collision guard + the `investigate`/`listen` verb-ownership collisions are routing-semantics decisions that belong with the **command-syntax-rework** lane, not a unilateral fix; the cosmetic doc-drift (README Python 3.11/107-tests, `pytest.ini` timeout comment, `Guide_06` frontmatter, arch `SCHEMA_VERSION` 43↔44) is left for a doc-hygiene pass; the design forks (non-credit value ledger, economy sim, persistent goal-stack) are flagged for a design deep-dive. All catalogued in `docs/design/06`.
- **Verified:** new `tests/test_newpassword_bcrypt.py` (3 — reset→authenticate round-trip, 6-char-min enforcement, fail-closed on a legacy SHA-256 hash) green; targeted regressions green — `test_smoke_foundation` + `test_smoke_telnet` (account-create + login), `test_smoke_movement`, `test_db_integrity`, `test_db_backup`, `test_chain_corpus_reachability_invariant` (35 total). AST-clean. **Gate before merge: `run_all_tests.bat` (Brian).**
- **Files:** `parser/mux_commands.py`, `db/database.py`, `parser/builtin_commands.py`, `tests/test_newpassword_bcrypt.py` (new), `CHANGELOG.md`, `TODO.json`.

### 2026-06-14 — Test-suite prune: activate the `slow` marker (inner-loop time lever) + cut verified dead weight — *drop test-suite-prune*
From a 21-group audit of the whole test suite (524 files / 9,416 tests / ~189K LOC; workflow `wa1ebxscp`). Headline: the suite is **healthy** — every subsystem group confirmed its engine symbols live (no phantom-symbol rot), and it makes **zero live LLM/network calls**, so its cost is **wall-clock, not API spend**. The cost is volume-driven (only ~14 files do heavy world-builds; sleeps are nearly absent), concentrated in a few mechanical patterns. So this drop is ~90% *repurpose*, ~10% *eliminate*.
- **The lever — activate the defined-but-unused `slow` marker.** `pytest.ini` shipped a `slow` marker that **zero** tests used. Now 1,366 of 9,416 tests are `slow` and deselected from the default inner loop (+240 smoke = 1,606 deselected; ~7,810 run by default). Tagged: the **entire SPA suite** (661 tests — every one spawns a Node.js subprocess; marked via new `tests/spa/conftest.py`, path-filtered + `tryfirst` so `-m` deselection actually applies) and **~37 heavy non-SPA files/classes** (full `build_mos_eisley`/`load_world_dry_run` world-builds, per-test in-memory-DB + full-migration files like `srb2`/`srb3`/`wow2-4`, Monte-Carlo loops in `combat_mechanics`/`session38`, `node --check`/subprocess-boot files, and client.html regex batteries). Mixed files got **class/method-level** markers to keep their fast majority in the inner loop (e.g. `f7c1` keeps 62 fast tests, drops 20 world-build).
- **Both configs, or it half-works.** There are two `[pytest]` configs — root `pytest.ini` (no-arg runs) and `tests/pytest.ini` (targeted `pytest tests/<module>` runs, i.e. the real inner loop, since pytest resolves the nearest inifile to the path arg). Added `-m "... and not slow"` to **both** addopts. The full gate (`run_all_tests.bat`, which clears addopts via `-o addopts=`) still runs **all 9,416** including smoke + slow. Logged the two-config smell as `TD.DUAL_PYTEST_INI`.
- **Eliminations (verified against HEAD, low-risk):** deleted the `tests/tests/` stale-duplicate tree (5 files from a mis-packaged `catchup_01` drop, already `collect_ignore`d — and removed that now-obsolete guard from `tests/conftest.py`); `tests/spa/combat_inspector_extract.py` (0-test pre-Drop-4.4 harness, superseded by `m3_combat_inspector_harness.py`, no importers); `tests/test_session46_ws_frame_parse.py` (20 tautological tests against a local `frame_to_text` stub that mirrors no production wire format — real server uses `{input:...}`); `tests/test_security_level_yaml_audit.py` (header self-declares "CLOSED by Drop S-RES"; superseded by `test_security_resolver_runtime.py` + `_writer_merge.py` + `test_security_zone_coverage.py`; one of its 2 tests only `warnings.warn`s). Pruned the `f7c1` `test_total_npc_count_includes_all_seven_village` brittle whole-table count canary (updated 10× — 145→…→211 — its own comment conceded "the by-name placement checks are the real guarantee," which are retained).
- **Deferred (logged, not lost):** sub-test fragment prunes (6 `TestDropMarker` self-asserts, `TestSilentExceptInvariant` in s39/s40 superseded by s38, `TestEncounterBoardingModule` s43↔s40 dup, `TestManualFidelityPin`, orphan_wireup xfails, `combat_extended` helper dup) + consolidate-parametrize candidates (gundark drops, NPC rosters, SPA tier-body static tests) → `TD.TEST_FRAGMENT_PRUNES_DEFERRED`.
- **Verified:** new `tests/test_slow_marker_contract.py` (self-enforcing guard: both configs exclude slow, the SPA conftest exists + only marks SPA, the deleted files stay deleted, the `slow` marker is actually used, the brittle canary is gone). Collection: default targeted/root runs deselect slow correctly (srb2→0, SPA→0, f7c1→62/82), an unmarked file is untouched by the SPA conftest, full `-o addopts=` collects all 9,416 with no collection errors; spot executions green (unmarked file 43/43; a SPA file under `-m slow` 4/4). **Gate before merge: `run_all_tests.bat` (Brian).**
- **Files:** `pytest.ini`, `tests/pytest.ini`, `tests/spa/conftest.py` (new), `tests/conftest.py`, `tests/test_slow_marker_contract.py` (new), `tests/test_f7c1_village_trials.py`, + `@pytest.mark.slow` on ~37 `tests/test_*.py`; deleted `tests/tests/` (5), `tests/spa/combat_inspector_extract.py`, `tests/test_session46_ws_frame_parse.py`, `tests/test_security_level_yaml_audit.py`; `CHANGELOG.md`, `TODO.json`.

### 2026-06-14 — Disk-persisted scheduler for the autonomous dev loop (durable_loop) — *drop durable-loop-scheduler*
Tooling (not game code): a disk-persisted scheduler so the unattended dev loop survives app-close / reboot / a compute-gap — the in-session `CronCreate` timers are session-only here and stalled an overnight run. `tools/durable_loop.py` wraps the OS-native **Windows Task Scheduler** (no reinvented daemon) to register a task that launches Claude Code HEADLESSLY (`claude -p`, resume prompt via stdin) in a chosen worktree, logging each run. Subcommands: `arm` (`--every N` recurring / `--in SEC` / `--at "YYYY-MM-DD HH:MM"` one-shot) · `list` · `status` (tail latest log) · `disarm`; plus `--dry-run` and `--test-fire`.
- **Durability is the OS scheduler's:** persisted to disk + kept alive by Windows; `MultipleInstancesPolicy=IgnoreNew` (a fire landing while a prior run is active is SKIPPED → never two claude sessions fighting over git); `StartWhenAvailable` (a fire missed during a gap runs when the box is back); `ExecutionTimeLimit=PT2H` (a hung run is killed). Auth inherits the user-scope `ANTHROPIC_API_KEY` (verified working headless on this box) — no secret is written by the tool.
- **Validated end-to-end:** unit tests for the launcher/XML/prompt builders + cross-platform `--dry-run`; a live self-test (`--test-fire`) armed a task, confirmed it PERSISTED in Task Scheduler, fired it on-demand, verified the run log, then disarmed + confirmed removed.
- **Use when instructed:** `python tools/durable_loop.py arm --every 20 --workdir C:/SW_MUSH_night`; `disarm` to stop. Default perm mode is `--dangerously-skip-permissions` (unattended git/tests need it) — arm only on a trusted repo. Codifies the durability lesson as the `no_passive_notification_wait` discipline.
- **Verified:** new `tests/test_durable_loop.py` (11) + live Task-Scheduler self-test. (No game-suite gate — tooling only, touches no game code.)
- **Files:** `tools/durable_loop.py` (new), `tests/test_durable_loop.py` (new), `CHANGELOG.md`, `TODO.json`.

### 2026-06-14 — T3.20 self-enforcing state-preservation contract; cluster COMPLETE (scope_notes f) — *drop state-preservation-contract*
Final T3.20 state-preservation slice (`scope_notes` f — "a written state-preservation contract that every future schema PR must honor; candidate arch invariant at the v52 consolidation"). New `docs/design/state_preservation_contract_v1.md` codifies five invariants (I1 reload-round-trip per persisted entity; I2 derived state reconstructs / never persists; I3 migrations forward-only + the `SCHEMA_VERSION==max(MIGRATIONS)` drift guard; I4 no orphans/corruption; I5 backup-before-migrate) + a PR checklist, referencing the real artifacts built across this cluster. `tests/test_state_preservation_contract.py` makes it SELF-ENFORCING: a static AST scan of engine/ai/db/server/parser finds every `from_dict`/`from_db_dict`/`from_json` deserializer and asserts the set equals a registry of round-trip-tested entities — so a NEW persisted serializer cannot ship without a round-trip guard. Also asserts serializer-pair symmetry, that every registered round-trip test file exists, and that the contract doc has no phantom artifact pointers. Test+doc only; collision-free; 5 tests.

### 2026-06-14 — T3.20 consistent online DB backup + restore/upgrade runbook (scope_notes d) — *drop db-backup-restore*
Fifth T3.20 state-preservation slice (`scope_notes` d — "Backup/restore + a documented upgrade runbook"). New `db/backup.py::backup_database(src, dst)` takes a CONSISTENT snapshot of a (possibly live) SQLite DB via SQLite's online backup API — no need to stop the game — returning the snapshot size and raising on failure (missing source / refused overwrite / SQLite error), so a silent 0-byte backup can't happen. Consumer: `tools/backup_db.py <src> <dst> [--overwrite] [--verify]`; `--verify` runs the integrity scanner (drop db-integrity-validator) against the snapshot and refuses to call a corrupt/orphaned backup good. `docs/design/backup_restore_runbook_v1.md` documents the backup → scan → migrate → scan loop (the AFTER scan catches a table-rebuild migration that orphaned rows) and the stop-server / file-replace / verify / restart restore.
- **Composes with the integrity validator:** backup + `--verify` is the state-preservation safety loop around any schema change (back up, scan, migrate, scan again).
- **Verified:** new `tests/test_db_backup.py` (5 — data preserved across a backup, online backup of a STILL-OPEN live DB, refuse-existing-dest vs `--overwrite`, missing-source raises, backup passes the integrity scan) + CLI smoke (`--verify` → OK/exit 0; refuse → 2; `--overwrite` → 0) + full-suite gate.
- **Files:** `db/backup.py` (new), `tools/backup_db.py` (new), `tests/test_db_backup.py` (new), `docs/design/backup_restore_runbook_v1.md` (new), `CHANGELOG.md`, `TODO.json`.
### 2026-06-14 — T3.20 round-trip lane completed: TrafficShip + NPCConfig (scope_notes c) — *drop serializer-roundtrip-extra*

(`to_dict`-only client serializers — area_loader, creature_special_attacks — have no deserializer, so no round trip to guard.)
