### 2026-06-13 — Equipment-instance accessor (Stage 1) + 2 live consumer-bug fixes — *drop 47*
Chips the `TD.EQUIPMENT_CHARACTER_HOLDS_KEYS_NOT_INSTANCES` debt with the lowest-risk slice, chosen from a full 5-surface seam map (98 read/write sites classified: only 4 genuinely need the instance, 2 of which drop 19/44 already thread). The Character holds equipped_weapon/worn_armor as bare KEY strings while the canonical DB column is per-slot ItemInstance JSON — so any consumer wanting condition/quality/crafter had to re-parse the JSON, which BLOCKS `CRAFT.powered_suit_design` + OBS armor Option C. **Additive accessor, NOT a field-type change** (the seam map found 56 key-only consumers that a type change would break) — "extend, don't add": reuses `read_equipment`, touches zero string contracts.
- **The accessor** (`engine/character.py`): new `_equipment_slots` field cached in `from_db_dict` from the `read_equipment` call it already makes (and now in `from_npc_sheet` too, so armed NPCs aren't None); read-only properties `equipped_weapon_inst` / `worn_armor_inst` expose the full ItemInstance. The bare-key fields + all 56 key-only consumers are untouched. Documented as a **load-time snapshot** (mirrors drop 44's `armor_soak_pips`).
- **Bug fix 1 — web HUD loadout was always blank** (`server/session.py::_build_loadout`): it read `name`/`damage`/`type` off the equipment JSON, but that's the `ItemInstance.to_dict()` shape (`key`/`condition`/`quality`/`crafter`) — those keys never existed, so the sidebar showed nothing. Now resolves the **name from the weapon registry by key**. (Emits ONLY `name` — the field the SPA actually consumes; richer condition/quality display is deferred to a drop that ships its SPA consumer too, to avoid a phantom-producer.)
- **Bug fix 2 — intel scans always reported "Unarmed"** (`engine/espionage.py::generate_scan_result`): it read `equipped_weapon`/`worn_armor` off the char DICT, but those are Character *attributes*, never dict columns — dead reads. Now reads the slot keys via `equipment_keys(char["equipment"])`, so espionage reports the real loadout.
- **Staleness fix (code-review)**: the 6 equip/wear/unequip/remove/repair/sell verbs mutate `char["equipment"]` but didn't drop the session's cached Character object, so its load-time snapshots (`_equipment_slots` AND drop 44's `armor_soak_pips`) went stale mid-session. Added `ctx.session.invalidate_char_obj()` after each — **also fixes drop 44's latent `armor_soak_pips` staleness**.
- **Phantom-producer fix (invariant-review)**: the first cut of `_build_loadout` emitted condition/quality/crafter/damage/type/protection_* that no SPA module reads — trimmed to the consumed `name` only.
- **Unblocks** `CRAFT.powered_suit_design` + OBS armor Option C — their rich-instance consumers can now read `char.worn_armor_inst.quality` instead of re-parsing JSON (their own design forks still gate the build). Bare-key retirement (Stage 3) stays deferred to T3.20.
- **Verified:** `tests/test_equipment_instance_accessor.py` (19 — accessor across all shapes + None safety + from_npc_sheet + the `_build_loadout` and espionage regression locks + bare-keys-untouched + armor_soak_pips coexistence) + 124-test equipment/inventory/session-HUD/espionage regression + the str-shape tests (equipment-untangle, gundark, social-force) stay green (additive contract). Reviewed: invariant-auditor + code-reviewer (both findings fixed). AST clean.
- **Files:** `engine/character.py`, `server/session.py`, `engine/espionage.py`, `parser/builtin_commands.py`, `tests/test_equipment_instance_accessor.py` (new), `tests/test_cities_phase4b.py` (mock completeness), `CHANGELOG.md`, `TODO.json`.

### 2026-06-13 — Ambient NPC life — Phase 0 DB scaffolding (pre-launch, inert) — *drop 46*
Lands the PRE-LAUNCH database scaffolding for T3.22 (ambient NPC life — idle-Ollama background world sim). Per the design doc (`ambient_npc_life_design_v1.md` §5-6) and Brian's live-safety requirement, the schema lands NOW (inert) so the post-launch sim build never migrates a live, populated DB. This drop is the ONLY part of the feature that touches the live DB, and it does so while it's safe. Nothing reads these tables yet — the sim (Phases 1-4) is post-launch.
- **Schema v44** (`db/database.py`): two new tables, in BOTH `SCHEMA_SQL` (fresh installs) AND `MIGRATIONS[44]` (existing-DB upgrade), all `CREATE TABLE IF NOT EXISTS` (idempotent, lowest-risk migration class — new empty tables, no ALTER on a hot table). `npc_ambient_state` (per-NPC goal/movement/activity runtime state, `npc_id` PK → `npcs(id)`, `current_room_id`/`dest_room_id` → `rooms(id)`, + `idx_npc_ambient_room`) and `npc_ambient_relationship` (NPC-NPC affinity, composite PK). Both carry a JSON `extra TEXT DEFAULT '{}'` future-proof blank — the SQLite-idiomatic "blank space" (new fields go into JSON with zero migration, like `characters.attributes`), per Brian's future-proofing instinct. Ambient config rides the existing `npcs.ai_config_json` (no schema change; `ambient_enabled` absent/false = every existing NPC unchanged — the key live-safety property).
- **Inert accessor stubs** (`db/database.py`, mirror the `cp_ticks` trio): `ambient_state_get` / `ambient_state_ensure_row` (INSERT OR IGNORE) / `ambient_state_update` (allowlisted columns) / `ambient_state_in_room` (the co-location query, uses the index). **NO callers yet** — shipped now so Phase 1 is pure feature code against present tables + accessors, with no DB-layer change racing a live player. A test asserts this inertness (no production reader).
- **Live-safety verified:** invariant-auditor CLEAN (confirmed the deliberate producer-without-consumer is the correct authorized pre-launch shape, not a phantom); smoke-verifier BOOTS CLEAN (227 smoke tests — `Database.initialize()` applies the v44 migration without error, full boot sequence clean).
- **Verified:** `tests/test_t3_22_ambient_life_phase0.py` (13 — version bump, migration 44 registered, both table shapes incl. the `extra` blank, the index, the v43→v44 upgrade path, idempotent re-run, accessor round-trip + FK enforcement + allowlist, the inertness guard) + 110-test schema/migration regression green. AST clean.
- **Files:** `db/database.py`, `tests/test_t3_22_ambient_life_phase0.py` (new), `CHANGELOG.md`, `TODO.json`.

### 2026-06-13 — xdist full-suite triage: 4 failures triaged, 3 stale-tests + 1 real silent-except fixed — *triage session*
Ran the full pytest suite under pytest-xdist (`-n auto`, 12 workers, ~8,800 items) per `HANDOFF_xdist_suite_triage_2026-06-13.md`, then triaged each failure real-bug-vs-bad-test single-threaded before touching anything. **4 distinct failures; 3 were tests drifted from correct/intended engine behavior, 1 was a real (minor) production silent-except.** Final suite: `8793 passed, 1 failed` — the lone red is purely two UNTRACKED guide-tool strays from the parallel guides-rework session (not this session's lane; flagged for Brian). No engine logic was wrong.

- **F4 — `test_session38::test_no_silent_except_pass_in_production` (1 REAL + 2 not-in-lane).** REAL: `parser/commissary_commands.py` had a bare `except: pass` swallowing a best-effort `shop_state` web push with no logging (`:197`), plus two comment-masked siblings the scanner missed (`:117`, `:146`). **Fixed all three** to `log.debug("[commissary] <list|buy|sell> shop_state push failed", exc_info=True)`, matching the bounty/inventory/crafting best-effort idiom. NOT-IN-LANE: two UNTRACKED guides-session tools (`guide_lint.py:39`, `split_guide_dev_track.py:35`) use the benign `sys.std*.reconfigure(encoding="utf-8")` console-bootstrap idiom; per Brian, flagged not touched — logged as `OBS.silent_except_invariant_reconfigure_carveout`.

(3) F2/F3 surfaced for the first time because drop 26 made `node_modules` repo-local-resolvable → jsdom now present → previously-skipped spa tests run.

### 2026-06-13 — Crafted consumable quality → potency (consumable half) — *drop 45*
Builds the CONSUMABLE half of `CRAFT.armor_consumable_quality_combat`, closing the last of the `OBS.quality_and_boosts` decoration gap (weapons drop-19, armor drop-44, consumables here). Crafted consumable quality was stored at craft time but discarded — only shown in the delivery message — so a q95 stimpack was mechanically identical to a vendor one. Design + balance analysis: `docs/design/consumable_quality_potency_v1.md` (written this session per Brian's "do a design doc first if you need it, don't stall"). Resolves the `CRAFT.consumable_quality_potency_model` fork on its recommended defaults.
- **Funnel (`engine/items.py::crafted_consumable_potency_pips`)** — TIGHTER than the weapon/armor band: cap **+1** (not +2), because a stim buff base is only +1D=3 pips, so even one pip is +33% and a +2 would push a q95 stim toward the next catalog tier (power creep). The whole good band (70-100) yields exactly +1; quality buys RELIABILITY of hitting +1, not magnitude. Takes a quality INT (consumables aren't ItemInstances — they store a per-key quality), reuses `_quality_band_pips`. Band: ≤49=-1, 50-69=0, 70-100=+1. Fail-open 0; vendor q50=0.
- **Storage migration (`engine/buffs.py`)** — consumables move from a bare int to `{"count", "quality"}`. New `_normalize_consumable_entry` coerces BOTH generations (legacy int → q50 vendor baseline; new dict as-is) so no DB migration script is needed — the read coerces lazily, the next write upgrades the shape (mirrors the equipment-column tolerance). `has_consumable`/`get_consumable_count`/`consume_consumable` route through it; `consume_consumable` PRESERVES the per-key quality on decrement and **stays a `bool`** (so its callers — `engine/breaching.py`, `parser/medical_commands.py` — keep their truthiness contract; no signature ripple). New `get_consumable_quality(char, key)` reads the per-key quality (the medic reads it before consuming). [Refines the design doc's "change consume_consumable's return type" to a separate reader — strictly less blast radius.]
- **Delivery write (`parser/crafting_commands.py`)** — persists quality alongside count, **max-on-recraft** (a better craft always upgrades the stack; quality is per-key since stims are fungible).
- **Potency hooks (`parser/medical_commands.py`)** — STIMS: scale the buff's `stat_modifiers` by the pip (floored at 0 so a shoddy stim is weaker but never a debuff) via an `add_buff(..., stat_modifiers=<scaled>)` override; q50→0 pip→template unchanged (vendor parity). MEDPACS: heal magnitude stays DISCRETE (1/2/1) — quality instead eases the First-Aid roll (lower effective difficulty = more reliable application), so a fine medpac applies cleanly more often without a balance-warping bigger heal; no double-dip (stims get magnitude, medpacs get reliability).
- **Power-creep guard (pinned):** a q95 stimpack reaches +1D+1 (4 pips) — strictly below `adrenaline_shot`'s +2D (6) vendor base, so the tier ladder holds. Asserted in `test_consumable_quality_potency.py::TestStimBuffScaling::test_q95_stim_below_next_tier`.
- **Migration regression:** the old `test_srb1b` assertion that post-consume storage is a bare int, and the `economy_progression` smoke assertion reading `consumables.medpac` as an int, were updated to read the count via `_normalize_consumable_entry` (tolerant of both shapes) — a legitimate test-update for the by-design storage change, not an engine fix.
- **Two code-review bugs caught + fixed pre-handback** (code-reviewer fan-out): (1) **`engine/buffs.py::add_buff` refresh path** silently dropped a `stat_modifiers` override when a buff of the same type already existed — so re-applying a higher-quality stim over an active one (the overdose path; all stims are `max_stacks=1` → always the refresh branch) kept the OLD magnitude. Now applies an EXPLICIT `stat_modifiers` override to the existing buff (template defaults still don't reset on a plain re-apply). (2) **delivery write used `int(quality)`** which truncated the `resolve_craft` float, so a craft displayed as "quality 70" (from 69.9) stored 69 → 0 pips instead of the +1 the player was shown; now `round(quality)` to match the displayed value and the band boundary. Both pinned by new tests (`TestAddBuffOverrideOnReapply`, `TestQualityRoundingAtBoundary`).
- **Verified:** `tests/test_consumable_quality_potency.py` (43 — funnel band/cap, normalizer both shapes incl. bool-not-count guard, quality-aware helpers, max-on-recraft, stim scaling + the tier-ladder invariant, + the 2 review-bug regressions) + `test_srb1b_stim_consumable_wiring` (updated) + `test_srb1_medic_stim` + `test_craft_p2_gundark_drop_a` (medpac heal UNCHANGED) + all `add_buff` consumers incl. `test_t2_10c_overdose_incap` green (132 combined) + AST clean + full xdist suite green modulo the 1 known not-mine guides-tool stray.
- **Files:** `engine/items.py`, `engine/buffs.py`, `parser/crafting_commands.py`, `parser/medical_commands.py`, `tests/test_consumable_quality_potency.py` (new), `tests/test_srb1b_stim_consumable_wiring.py`, `tests/smoke/scenarios/economy_progression.py`, `docs/design/consumable_quality_potency_v1.md` (new), `CHANGELOG.md`, `TODO.json`.

### 2026-06-13 — Crafted armor quality → combat soak (armor half) — *drop 44*
Builds the ARMOR half of `CRAFT.armor_consumable_quality_combat` (Brian-greenlit: "quality should absolutely matter"). Closes the armor side of the half-closed `OBS.quality_and_boosts` decoration gap that the crafting-integration review flagged: a crafted q95 vest used to soak EXACTLY like a vendor/q40 one because `get_armor_protection` read only the bare `worn_armor` KEY (the instance quality was discarded by `from_db_dict`). Mirrors the ratified Drop-19 weapon precedent (`crafted_combat_pips`), hard-capped to forbid power creep.
- **Funnel (`engine/items.py::crafted_armor_soak_pips`)** — the armor sibling of `crafted_combat_pips`, in the same documented "ONLY places crafted quality becomes a combat number" funnel block. Reuses `_quality_band_pips` VERBATIM (≤49=-1, 50-69=0, 70-89=+1, 90-100=+2) so armor and weapons share one band boundary. Cap `max(-1, min(2, ...))` — naturally +2 (not the weapon's +3=+1D), because armor has NO experiment-mod axis in the registry (`weapons.yaml` carries only `protection_energy`/`protection_physical`, no `protection_mod`), so there's no boost term. Returns int (one combat axis: soak), vs the weapon's (dmg, acc) tuple. Fail-open: 0 for None/non-instance; vendor q50 = 0.
- **Producer (`engine/character.py::from_db_dict`)** — computes the soak pip ONCE at load, where the equipment JSON is still in hand (it's discarded past this point), and caches it as a new primitive `Character.armor_soak_pips: int = 0`. Mirrors the Drop-19 weapon-pip isolation (combat never re-reads equipment). Switched the equipment read from `equipment_keys` to a single `read_equipment` call (keys derived from the same slots — no double-parse). `from_db_dict` is the UNIVERSAL Character construction path (players via `session.get_char_obj`, DB NPCs via `Character.from_db_dict`), so one producer site covers every combat participant; `invalidate_char_obj` after `save_character` means re-equipping recomputes.
- **Consumer (`engine/combat.py::_apply_damage`)** — folds `target.armor_soak_pips` into `armor_pool` BEFORE Strength-add and BEFORE the wound penalty, only when the armor already protects against this damage type (`not armor_pool.is_zero()`), so quality AMPLIFIES existing protection rather than conjuring soak for a damage type the armor doesn't cover (e.g. a +pip on an energy-only vest does not soak a melee hit). `DicePool + int` carries pips (3 = +1D). The structured `soak_armor_pool` inspector event auto-reflects the delta (folded before emit). `get_armor_protection` itself is UNCHANGED — so `test_craft_p2_gundark_drop_c`'s registry soak-row pins stay green (the delta lives in combat, not the registry read).
- **Cap rationale:** +2/floor -1 mirrors the weapon quality band Brian already ratified; soak adds alongside Strength so the conservative band is the power-creep-safe choice.
- **Consumable half deferred** to a follow-up drop with its own design doc (the potency model is a genuine power-creep balance fork — pip-delta-on-base vs quality-factor — plus medpac-scaling and a bare-int→quality-dict storage migration; Brian: "do a design doc/analysis first if you need it, don't stall").
- **Verified:** `tests/test_craft_armor_soak_quality.py` (25 — funnel bands/cap/fail-open, producer captures pip from equipment JSON across all 3 historical shapes, consumer q95>q40 soak incl. physical, registry path unchanged) + `test_obs_quality_combat` (50) + `test_craft_p2_gundark_drop_c` (20) regression green + AST clean.
- **Files:** `engine/items.py`, `engine/character.py`, `engine/combat.py`, `tests/test_craft_armor_soak_quality.py` (new), `CHANGELOG.md`, `TODO.json`.

Neither blind-integrated (HIGH combat-file collision + balance judgment).

### 2026-06-13 — Breaching charges (breach verb + demolitions check) — *drop 40*
Builds the breaching half of CRAFT.mines_breaching_split (Brian greenlit the split — build breaching, defer placed mines). A `breach <target>` verb blows open a sealed obstacle with a single-use breaching charge and a Demolitions check vs the obstacle's difficulty. Safe by design (breaches obstacles, not people — no blast-on-players); placed proximity mines remain a separate deferred subsystem.
- **Engine core** (`engine/breaching.py::attempt_breach`, mirrors `engine/housing.py::attempt_force_door`): finds a `breachable` room object (type `breachable`, `data.breach_difficulty`), requires + consumes a breaching charge (via `engine.buffs.consume_consumable` — the charge is a crafted consumable in `attributes.consumables`, spent on the ATTEMPT whether or not it succeeds, grenade single-use precedent), runs `perform_skill_check("demolitions", difficulty)`, and on success deletes the obstacle and reveals its `data.reveal` flavor. Failure-tolerant throughout (`find_breachable` handles no-target / ambiguous / mismatch).
- **`breach` command** (`parser/demolitions_commands.py`, new; registered in `game_server.py` + the reachability-test registry): thin front end + a room broadcast of the blast on success.
- **Craftable breaching charge:** `breaching_charge` schematic (Demolitions, diff 17, taught by Kayson) → `output_type: consumable` + a `data/consumables.yaml` identity row (category `ordnance`). The three-way consumable-parity invariant (`test_craft_p2_gundark_drop_a`) was extended with a `NON_STIM_CONSUMERS` allow-set documenting where the non-stim mechanic lives (`engine/breaching.py`) — so the "no inert consumable tokens" rule stays honest while allowing a non-stim consumer.
- **No blast-on-players, no new faucet** (the charge is a crafted sink-side item). **Placed mines deferred.**
- **Open call logged** — `CRAFT.breaching_obstacle_placement`: no world-data object-seeding path exists today, so breachable obstacles are admin/builder-placeable now but not yet authored at scale; the seeding-vs-exit-gating placement path is a pending design call. The MECHANIC is complete + tested regardless.
- **Verified:** `tests/test_breaching.py` (9 — find_breachable matching, charge gate, consume-on-attempt for success AND failure, obstacle deletion, no-obstacle/mismatch paths) + the consumable-parity invariant + reachability invariant + smoke green.

### 2026-06-13 — Commissary sellback model (anti-laundering refund + bind-to-channel) — *drop 38*
Resolves the ECON.commissary_sellback design call in full (all 3 pieces — Brian ratified incl. same-faction trade). Faction-issued / commissary gear can no longer be bought at the requisition discount and resold on the open market for profit (the laundering loop), and it stays within its issuing faction.
- **Piece 1 — vendor refusal (the anti-laundering lock):** `engine/items.py::npc_refuses_buyback` now also refuses any `faction_issued` item (was crafted-quality-only). Works on both ItemInstance and plain inventory dicts (new `_item_attr` shim). Ordinary vendors hand faction gear back. (The vendor-droid path already refused it — this closes the NPC-vendor `sell` path too.)
- **Piece 2 — the commissary refund channel:** `engine/commissary.py::sell_commissary` + `+commissary sell <key>`. Faction gear sells back ONLY to the issuing faction's commissary, refunding `COMMISSARY_SELLBACK_RATE` (50%) of the item's requisition cost via the metered `commissary_sellback` faucet — BY CONSTRUCTION smaller than the `commissary_purchase` sink that created it, so the buy→sellback round trip is a strict NET LOSS (pinned by `TestNoLaunderingLoop`). The requisition cost is now stamped on the item at purchase (`requisition_cost`), with a stock-price fallback for legacy items. Refund-safe ordering (remove item, then credit; restore on credit failure). Channel-bound: you sell Republic gear to the Republic commissary, not the Hutts'.
- **Piece 3 — bind-to-channel transfer:** `engine/items.py::faction_bound_transfer_blocked` gates `give` (PC→PC) and `trade` so faction-issued gear only transfers to a SAME-FACTION member (intra-faction redistribution is lore-apt + laundering-neutral; outsiders refused). NPC hand-off unaffected (consumed). Items without a `faction_code` fall back to not-blocked (the vendor lock is the real laundering guard).
- **Faucet/sink:** the only new tag is the `commissary_sellback` faucet, paired with + smaller than the existing `commissary_purchase` sink. Routed through `adjust_credits` (auto-visible on `@economy`).
- **Verified:** `tests/test_commissary_sellback.py` (18 — all 3 pieces incl. the net-loss invariant, wrong-channel refusal, legacy stock fallback, refund-safe restore) + 110-test commissary/buyback/vendor-sell/give/trade/builtin regression green + smoke.
- **Files:** `engine/items.py`, `engine/commissary.py`, `parser/commissary_commands.py`, `parser/builtin_commands.py`, `tests/test_commissary_sellback.py`, `CHANGELOG.md`, `TODO.json`.

### 2026-06-13 — World-event flag consumers (3 of 5): distress + hutt_auction + brawl — *drop 37*
Completes the WORLDEVENT.flag_effect_consumers gap — all 5 dead world-event FLAG effects now have thin consumers over existing systems (the design call is now fully resolved). Same pattern throughout: a pure modulator (unit-tested without the manager) read at one existing seam.
- **`distress_active` (DISTRESS_SIGNAL → mission board):** `engine/missions.py::distress_mission_bonus` (+30% emergency pay, `DISTRESS_REWARD_BONUS`). In `generate_mission`, while the signal is live, the rolled type is forced to MEDICAL (a distress call IS a medical/rescue job), the reward gets the premium, and the title becomes "DISTRESS: <dest>". Mirrors the existing Director-alert-level bias in `_pick_type`.
- **`hutt_auction` (HUTT_AUCTION → rep-gated rare purchase):** per the design call's "SIMPLIFY to a rep-gated purchase, NOT bidding." `engine/world_events.py::hutt_auction_purchase_allowed` (gate: active AND hutt_cartel rep ≥ the event's `criminal_rep_gate`, default 30) + `apply_hutt_auction_markup` (+40%). Wired into the buy command (`parser/space_commands.py`): while a Hutt auction is live, an eligible criminal can buy a normally-UNSTOCKED item (the ONLY bypass of the market-segmentation gate) at the auction markup. Fail-closed — any error falls through to the normal refusal, never accidentally opens the gate. (`char` assignment moved up a few lines so the async rep check can live in the refusal branch; no behavior change to the existing path.)
- **`brawl_active` (CANTINA_BRAWL → the d66 cantina table):** `engine/cantina_encounters.py::roll_cantina_encounter(brawl_active=…)` forces the barroom-brawl beat (code 12) on a random `+cantina` roll while the event is live (the brawl is literally happening). Explicit `+cantina <code>` is unaffected.
- **No new faucets:** distress rides the existing mission-reward faucet (bonus on an existing payout); hutt_auction is a SINK (a premium-priced purchase); brawl is pure flavor-table steering.
- **Verified:** `tests/test_worldevent_flag_consumers.py` now 26 (all 5 flags — pure modulators incl. edge/fail-closed cases + manager-driven flag paths incl. `generate_mission` forcing MEDICAL) + the market-segmentation source-pin made robust (order invariant, not a brittle char-window) + 268-mission/bounty/scene/market/vendor regression green.
- **Files:** `engine/missions.py`, `engine/world_events.py`, `engine/cantina_encounters.py`, `parser/space_commands.py`, `parser/scene_commands.py`, `tests/test_worldevent_flag_consumers.py`, `tests/test_econ_market_segmentation.py`, `CHANGELOG.md`, `TODO.json`.

First two of the five dead world-event FLAG effects get thin consumers, per the WORLDEVENT.flag_effect_consumers design call (build one flag per increment; extend-don't-add over existing systems, mirroring the contraband_scan precedent — read the flag at one seam, modulate a deterministic outcome).

Failure-tolerant (flag-lookup hiccup → unchanged price).

Consumed in `generate_bounty` right after `_pick_tier()`. SUPERIOR contracts unchanged; failure-tolerant.

Ungated schematics + existing trainers are unaffected.

Final band: every onboarding chain lands a player at **recognized (~8–13)** in its faction — "the faction knows your name," ~10% of max — and "The Hermit's Trial" lands jedi_order = 18. NO chain reaches honored (50) or even mid-trusted; the t5 lightsaber's rep-50 gate must be earned through post-questline play (questline gate and rep floor stay SEPARATE). Pinned by `TestChainRepEconomyCeiling` (hard ceiling 22 + no-honored + questline-leaves-room-to-climb).
- **Achievement** `hermits_trial` added to `data/achievements.yaml` (the questline grants it on graduation; was a phantom producer until cataloged — caught by `test_drop_f8c2e`).

### 2026-06-13 — T5-questline arc Drop A: multi-slot chain engine + `mastery` surface — *drop 33*
Engine groundwork for the master-trainer questlines (`T2.DEF.t5_trainer_storyline`, design in `docs/design/t5_trainer_questlines_design_v1.md`). The chain engine was single-slot + chargen-only (`attributes.tutorial_chain`, no start-verb). This drop generalizes it to support a SECOND, deliberately-started mid-game questline slot — behavior-neutral for onboarding (all 222 legacy chain tests green). No content yet; Drop B authors the 5 questlines + trainers.
- **Multi-slot state machine** (`engine/tutorial_chains.py`): every state helper (`select_chain`, `get_current_step`, `advance_step`, `is_chain_complete`, `get_active_chain_id`, `reset_chain_state`, `get_satisfied_prereqs`, `record_prereq_satisfied`, `clear_step_progress`, `record_combat_kills`, `get_combat_kills`) gains an optional `state_key` param defaulting to `_TUTORIAL_CHAIN_KEY` — so legacy onboarding callers are byte-for-byte unchanged. New `_QUESTLINE_KEY = "active_questline"` slot + `CHAIN_STATE_KEYS` tuple. New `has_completed_chain(attrs, chain_id)` durable graduated-marker check (used by the Drop-B curriculum gate).
- **`kind` chain field** (default `"tutorial"`; `"questline"` validated against `ALLOWED_CHAIN_KINDS`): additive — an absent `kind:` loads as `tutorial`, so no existing chain YAML changes. The chargen picker (`engine/creation_wizard.py`) now skips `kind: questline` chains entirely (questlines are mid-game, never chargen-assigned).
- **Slot-aware dispatcher** (`engine/chain_events.py`): `_get_active_step`, `_try_advance`, and `get_active_step_info` take a `state_key`; the 11 public hooks now route through a new `_try_advance_all_slots` that walks every slot (onboarding + questline) so one runtime event advances whichever slot owns the matching step. The multi-enemy combat-tally pre-check accumulates per-slot. Failure-tolerant per slot.
- **Slot-aware teleport/pending-flag** (`engine/chain_graduation.py`): `apply_graduation`, `apply_step_teleport`, and `_clear_pending` take a `state_key`; `execute_pending_teleport` walks BOTH slots for a pending flag. Without this a questline's inter-step/graduation teleport would have stamped `pending_step_room_id` onto a veteran's *graduated onboarding* block — slot corruption. (Caught by the code-reviewer fan-out; fixed + regression-pinned in `TestTeleportSlotIsolation` before commit.)
- **Mid-game questline surface** (`engine/chain_events.py` + `parser/questline_commands.py`): `list_questlines` / `get_questline_offer` / `start_questline` / `abandon_questline` / `has_active_questline` back the new **`mastery`** command (`mastery [start <id> | status | abandon]`). Verb is `mastery` (NOT `quest`/`quests`/`train` — those keys are owned by the Director-AI personal-quest system, the spacer quest, and the CP-spend/tutorial `train`; collision-checked). One questline at a time; eligibility reuses `is_chain_locked_for_character` (the rep/faction gate). NPC-offer surface rides the existing `talk_to_npc` hook — talking to a questline's start-NPC while eligible surfaces "Type `mastery start <id>`".
- **Verified:** `tests/test_t5_questline_engine.py` (24 — slot parameterization + isolation, per-slot combat tally, the `kind` field + invalid-kind rejection, the full start/abandon/offer/one-at-a-time surface, the dispatcher's both-slot walk, onboarding-only-char neutrality, teleport/graduation slot-isolation regression, offer-prefers-unlocked) + the 298-test chain regression (test_f8c2b*, test_f8_*, test_f7j_*, chargen chain-selection, chain_graduation, reachability invariant) all green + smoke suite (227 passed).
- **Files:** `engine/tutorial_chains.py`, `engine/chain_events.py`, `engine/chain_graduation.py`, `engine/creation_wizard.py`, `parser/npc_commands.py`, `parser/questline_commands.py` (new), `server/game_server.py`, `docs/design/t5_trainer_questlines_design_v1.md` (new), `tests/test_t5_questline_engine.py` (new), `CHANGELOG.md`, `TODO.json`.

### 2026-06-13 — Newbie-friendly get / take / drop redirect stubs — *drop 32*
Closes the drop-24 onboarding handoff's deferred P2.4. A new player reflexively types `get <x>` / `take <x>` / `drop <x>` (verbs from every other text game), and hit a dead-end "Huh? Unknown command." SW_MUSH has no ground-item system — items come from examining the world, commissaries/shops, loot, and crafting; a free-standing ground get/drop is a deliberate DESIGN NON-goal, not an oversight. These purely-additive redirect stubs replace the dead-end with a helpful pointer to the real mechanics.
- **`GetTakeCommand`** (`get` + aliases `take`/`pickup`/`grab`): "There's nothing here to pick up" → points at `examine`, `buy` (commissary/shop), `loot`, `+craft`, and `give` (to receive a hand-off). 
- **`DropStubCommand`** (`drop` + alias `discard`): "You can't drop items on the ground here" → points at `sell`, `unequip`, `give`.
- Pure redirects: no state change, no ground-item system, no collision with existing commands (`loot`/`give`/`sell` intact; verified). Registered in `register_all`.
- **Verified:** `tests/test_get_drop_redirect_stubs.py` (aliases resolve, no clobber of existing builtins, help text points at the real acquisition/disposal paths) + 112-test builtin regression green.
- **Files:** `parser/builtin_commands.py`, `tests/test_get_drop_redirect_stubs.py` (new), `CHANGELOG.md`, `TODO.json`.

### 2026-06-13 — DIFF.4: threat-band reward scaling at the bounty payout — *drop 31*
The reward gradient that makes difficulty tiers matter economically. Per difficulty_tiers_design_v1.md §7.
- **Band multiplier at the bounty payout** (`parser/bounty_commands.py::BountyCollectCommand`): the payout now scales by the threat band of where the TARGET was (`contract.target_room_id`, bound in drop 26) — hunting a mark in the Deep Wilds pays the danger premium (2.0×), running down a Frontier-zone target pays 0.6×. So a veteran can't farm newbie contracts for full rate, and pushing into higher bands is the natural income gradient. Inserted right before the metered `bounty` `adjust_credits` faucet, mirroring the existing `bounty_reward_mult` surge pattern — rides the SAME faucet (no new credit source, faucet discipline intact). Surfaces a "Danger premium (Deep Wilds): +N credits" / "Low-threat contract (Frontier): -N credits" line. Failure-tolerant: a contract with no bound room (legacy/unbound) or any error leaves the reward unscaled (×1.0).
- **Economist's note:** the multipliers (0.6/1.0/1.4/2.0) are the design's first-guess tunables — post-launch telemetry tunes them. Applied only at the bounty faucet for now (the design's named lever + the cleanest difficulty→reward link, since the target's room band is unambiguous). Mission/encounter reward scaling can extend the same `reward_multiplier(band)` helper in a follow-up if telemetry shows the gradient needs more surface.
- **Verified:** `tests/test_diff4_bounty_band_multiplier.py` (structural pin — multiplier wired before the faucet, rides the existing `bounty` faucet; math — band→× mapping, Wilds pays >3× a Frontier contract) + `test_e2_dormant_effects` (the surge-multiplier ordering pin still holds) + 207-test bounty regression green.
- **Files:** `parser/bounty_commands.py`, `tests/test_diff4_bounty_band_multiplier.py` (new), `CHANGELOG.md`, `TODO.json`.

---

### 2026-06-13 — DIFF.3: tiered wilderness-encounter eligibility by threat band — *drop 30*
The first GAMEPLAY-impacting difficulty-tiers phase: the threat band now gates which encounters a wilderness tile can roll. Per difficulty_tiers_design_v1.md §6.
- **Band eligibility on encounter entries** (`engine/wilderness_encounters.py`): `EncounterEntry` gains `min_band` / `max_band` (numeric ratings, default 1..4 = eligible everywhere — an un-banded pool is unchanged). `_filter_pool` gates an entry out of a tile whose band rating is outside `[min_band, max_band]`: a Frontier tile (rating 1) draws only the trivial fauna / low-tier hostiles; a Deep Wilds tile (rating 4) unlocks the minibosses gated out everywhere else. The loader (`parse_encounter_pool`) parses + clamps to [1,4] + normalizes a reversed pair to "eligible everywhere" (a typo can't silently zero an entry).
- **Band resolved at the move seam** (`parser/builtin_commands.py` wilderness-move): the destination tile's threat band is resolved once (`get_effective_threat(...).rating`) and threaded into `roll_encounter` → `_filter_pool`. Failure-tolerant — a read error resolves to the Settled default (rating 2), so a hiccup never breaks a move.
- **Authored band bounds on the shipped corpus** (additive, 3 insertions each): the dangerous tier-2 encounters now carry `min_band: 3` — Coruscant Underworld `maze_ambush` (Maze predators) and Dune Sea `tusken_war_party` (six-rider war party). Verified end-to-end against the real pool: maze_ambush is gated OUT at band 1 and eligible at band 3. (Both regions are currently band-3 zones, so the encounters still fire there; the gating becomes differentiating the moment Frontier/Wilds sub-tiles are carved — the framework is now live.)
- **Bonus fix — pre-existing flaky test root-caused + fixed** (`tests/test_session38.py::test_security_scaling`): asserted `lawless > secured` texture-encounter triggers but used the GCW zones `corellia_orbit`/`kessel_approach` which aren't in the CW `engine.npc_space_traffic.ZONES` map (post GCW-retirement), so `_texture_trigger_probability` fell back to the base prob for BOTH → a pure RNG coin-flip that failed consistently. Retargeted to real CW zones (`coruscant_orbit` 0.005 vs `nar_shaddaa_orbit` 0.010); now deterministic 3/3. (`TD.FLAKY_TEXTURE_SECURITY_SCALING` opened + resolved same drop.)
- **DIFF.4 (reward multiplier) deferred to its own drop:** the `reward_multiplier(band)` helper + tests already shipped in DIFF.1, but wiring it into specific credit faucets (bounty/mission/encounter payouts) touches the economy and deserves a focused economy-review pass rather than riding the spawn-gating drop. The mechanism is ready; the faucet wiring is the next phase.
- **Verified:** `tests/test_diff3_encounter_band_eligibility.py` (12 — defaults, the gating filter at every band, loader parse/clamp/normalize, authored bounds present) + the full encounter/wilderness regression (631 passed, 0 failed — including the now-fixed texture test).
- **Files:** `engine/wilderness_encounters.py`, `parser/builtin_commands.py`, `data/worlds/clone_wars/wilderness/coruscant_underworld.yaml`, `data/worlds/clone_wars/wilderness/dune_sea.yaml`, `tests/test_diff3_encounter_band_eligibility.py` (new), `tests/test_session38.py`, `CHANGELOG.md`, `TODO.json`.

### 2026-06-13 — DIFF.2: threat-band zone labeling + look header tag + `+threat` — *drop 29*
The second difficulty-tiers phase — makes the DIFF.1 axis VISIBLE. Per difficulty_tiers_design_v1.md §5/§8.
- **Zone labeling pass** (`data/worlds/clone_wars/zones.yaml`, purely additive — 37 insertions, 0 deletions): every CW zone now carries `properties.threat_band` per the design's per-world tier map. Frontier (newbie) on the chain starting zones + secured cores (Kamino Tipoca, Geonosis foundries, Tatooine/Kuat spaceports, Coruscant monumental/senate/temple, Kamino/space-core lanes); Settled mid-game; Contested Marches on the lawless fringes (outskirts, undercity, barracks, deep hive, ocean platform, deep-space lanes); Deep Wilds on the end-game wilderness (Dune Sea, Nar Shaddaa warrens, Geonosis Ey'akh). All four bands are used (the gradient is real); no zone violates frontier≠lawless (the lawless bounty_hunter start at nar_shaddaa_promenade is Settled, not Frontier).
- **`look` room-header tag** (`parser/builtin_commands.py::_room_header`): the band renders as a color-graded `[FRONTIER]` / `[CONTESTED MARCHES]` / `[DEEP WILDS]` tag alongside the existing security tag — so "players see where the tiers are" (the KNOWN lines Brian asked for). Settled (the default) is suppressed to keep the common-case header quiet. Resolves through the same `get_room_property` zone-inheritance chain security uses; failure-tolerant (a read error just drops the tag).
- **`+threat` command** (alias `threat`, `parser/builtin_commands.py::ThreatCommand`): the dedicated "tell me more" surface — band name + level (N/4) + a one-line "what this means" blurb. Read-only; no state.
- **Verified:** `tests/test_diff1_threat_band.py` + `tests/test_diff2_zone_bands.py` (26 unit — every zone has a valid band, security property intact, no frontier≠lawless conflict, starting zones are frontier/settled, all four bands used); `tests/smoke/test_smoke_threat_band.py` (3 runtime — look shows/suppresses the tag, +threat + alias render); **full smoke suite 227 green, boots clean, zero regressions** (smoke-verifier); invariant-auditor clean (additive YAML confirmed, era-clean, real consumer, no funnel touched). Still behavior-neutral on the GAMEPLAY side — the bands are surfaced but don't yet gate spawns (DIFF.3) or scale rewards (DIFF.4).
- **Files:** `data/worlds/clone_wars/zones.yaml`, `parser/builtin_commands.py`, `tests/test_diff2_zone_bands.py` (new), `tests/smoke/scenarios/threat_band.py` (new), `tests/smoke/test_smoke_threat_band.py` (new), `CHANGELOG.md`, `TODO.json`.

### 2026-06-13 — Difficulty tiers DESIGN + DIFF.1 engine axis (threat bands) — *drop 28*
Resolves the DESIGN half of `T2.DIFF.difficulty_tiers_design` (the six open sub-decisions + a design doc) and ships DIFF.1, the behavior-neutral engine foundation. Direction was approved (extend security-zone + wilderness machinery, no parallel system); the six sub-decisions are made in `docs/design/difficulty_tiers_design_v1.md` with my senior-designer judgment per Brian's standing "press on design" directive (a few tunables + the band names flagged for his call, non-blocking).
- **Design doc** (`docs/design/difficulty_tiers_design_v1.md`): the load-bearing insight is that **difficulty ≠ security** — security says *whether* combat/PvP is allowed, the new threat band says *how dangerous* the enemies are; they're orthogonal axes on a zone (conflating them would force every newbie zone SECURED, killing the "newbies fight in a newbie area" requirement). Resolves: (1) four named bands w/ numeric backing — **Frontier(1) / Settled(2) / Contested Marches(3) / Deep Wilds(4)**; (2) separate orthogonal axis; (3) advisory by default + one soft confirm-gate for the Deep Wilds (no level locks — D6 has no levels); (4) a per-world tier map over the 6 launch worlds (mostly a labeling pass over existing zones — chain starts = Frontier, PC cities Settled+, end-game in the wilderness edges); (5) space lanes get the same bands via the same filter; (6) frontier≠lawless hard constraint + a threat-band reward multiplier through the existing `adjust_credits` faucet so veterans can't farm newbie zones. Tiered spawn rides the EXISTING wilderness encounter pools' `tier:` labels (made load-bearing via additive `min_band/max_band` eligibility) — no creature re-statting. 5-phase build plan (DIFF.1–5).
- **DIFF.1 engine axis** (`engine/threat_band.py`, new): `ThreatBand` enum (rating 1-4, default SETTLED), `get_effective_threat(room_id, db)` resolving via the SAME `db.get_room_property` zone-inheritance chain security uses (room→zone→parent-zone→default), player-facing display helpers (`threat_label` ANSI tag, `threat_name`, `threat_blurb`, `threat_color_code` for the map overlay), `frontier_lawless_conflict` validator, and the `reward_multiplier` band→×mapping (DIFF.4 consumes it). Failure-tolerant: a difficulty read never raises (a DB hiccup resolves to the default, never breaks look/move).
- **World-loader validation** (`engine/world_loader.py::validate_world`): new check #7 — a zone/room declaring BOTH `threat_band: frontier` AND `security: lawless` is a load error (the only hard coupling of the two axes; a newbie zone can't be a free-fire zone). Reads from zone/room `raw.properties`. The live CW world (no threat tags yet) validates clean — DIFF.1 ships with default SETTLED everywhere, so ZERO behavior change until DIFF.2 labels zones.
- **Verified:** `tests/test_diff1_threat_band.py` (20 tests — enum/parsing, resolver w/ zone-inheritance + failure-tolerance, display helpers, the validator, reward multiplier monotonicity, AND the live-world-validates-clean pin); foundation smoke green (boots clean); world-loader validation tests green.
- **Files:** `engine/threat_band.py` (new), `engine/world_loader.py`, `docs/design/difficulty_tiers_design_v1.md` (new), `docs/design/INDEX.md`, `tests/test_diff1_threat_band.py` (new), `CHANGELOG.md`, `TODO.json`.

### 2026-06-13 — B3 era sweep of the help corpus + SPA DOM tests unblocked — *drop 27*
Closes the help-corpus half of `T2.CW.codebase_era_sweep` (the prior sweeps covered engine/parser/server + data-worlds but never the `data/help/` markdown corpus, which is NOT era-gated — it loads via engine/help_loader.py + server/web_portal.py for ALL eras, so Clone Wars players were seeing Original-Trilogy / GCW terms in live help text).
- **Help-corpus era sweep** (~50 replacements across 21 files under `data/help/`): re-skinned OT/GCW flavor to Clone Wars equivalents while preserving every WEG D6 mechanic, dice code, command syntax, and number. Stormtrooper→clone trooper/battle droid; Imperial/Empire→Republic; Rebel/Alliance/Rebellion→Separatist/CIS/Confederacy; X-Wing→ARC-170/V-19; TIE→Vulture droid; Star Destroyer→Venator-class; AT-ST/AT-AT→AT-TE/spider droid; Death Star→Battlestation; canon OT figures used as examples (Han Solo, Millennium Falcon)→generic archetypes (a hard-bitten smuggler, a YT-1300 freighter). Mos Eisley / Tatooine kept (both are CW-era) with their OT-specific surroundings re-skinned (Imperial garrison → Republic security post). Files: +bounty/+bridge/+combat/+faction/+home/+mission/+perform/+pilot/+quest/+sabacc/+sensors/+ship/+smuggle/+spy command help + anomalies/capital/hyperdrive/moseisley/scale/smuggling/tatooine/transponder topics. 378 help tests green; all 70 help entries reload clean.
- **3 more B3 violations in code/data** (the era-sweep item's flagged `attack han` example + 2 found by an audit): `parser/combat_commands.py` `attack han`→`attack thug`/`attack raider` help examples; `data/help_topics.py` scale table (AT-ST/X-Wing/Star Destroyer/Death Star → AT-TE/V-19/Venator/Battlestation) + the capital-ship help passage; `engine/creation_wizard.py` chargen "mercenary as Han Solo at the start of A New Hope" → a generic "hard-bitten smuggler running spice off Nar Shaddaa". ("Sith Lord" in organizations.yaml left as-is: `npc_only: true`, never player-reachable, and Sith Lords ARE canonically present in 20 BBY.)
- **SPA DOM test suite unblocked** (`tests/spa/spa_dom_harness.py` + `tests/spa/m3_combat_inspector_harness.py`): the jsdom-backed SPA tests hardcoded `/tmp/node_modules` and SKIPPED everywhere jsdom wasn't manually installed there (every dev box) — so a whole tier of web-client DOM coverage was silently dormant. The harnesses now resolve `node_modules` dynamically, preferring the repo-local `node_modules/` (where jsdom actually lives, installed by the VSCode extension's npm), falling back to `/tmp/node_modules`. The SPA DOM tests now run for anyone with the repo deps — no manual setup. Activating them surfaced + fixed one latent test-selector bug: `tests/spa/test_m3_shop.py::test_vendor_mode_renders_commissary_panel` used `querySelector('.shop-tag-unplaced')` which returns the FIRST unplaced tag (a 'short' row) when the fixture has both a 'short' and a 'rank' row — now collects ALL tag texts so the rank assertion finds the rank tag (product was always correct; the selector was ambiguous).
- **Verified:** 378 help tests + 11 onboarding/shop SPA DOM tests green; help corpus reloads clean; final grep confirms zero OT/Imperial live terms remain in data/help/.
- **Files:** `data/help/commands/*.md` (14), `data/help/topics/*.md` (8), `data/help_topics.py`, `parser/combat_commands.py`, `engine/creation_wizard.py`, `tests/spa/spa_dom_harness.py`, `tests/spa/m3_combat_inspector_harness.py`, `tests/spa/test_m3_shop.py`, `CHANGELOG.md`, `TODO.json`.

### 2026-06-13 — Onboarding polish: tutorial bounty binding, examine room NPCs/objects, web NEXT line — *drop 26*
The P2 non-blocking onboarding polish from the drop-24 audit, plus 2 real bugs surfaced while building it and a test-isolation fix.
- **Tutorial bounty target binding** (`engine/chain_missions.py::_spawn_bounty`): `_materialize_bounty` left `target_npc_id`/`target_room_id` = None; the tutorial_bounties.yaml entry carries `target_room_slug` which the materializer ignored, so `bountytrack` hard-errored "Contract data error — target NPC not found" on the tutorial Tarko Vinn contract. `_spawn_bounty` now resolves `target_room_slug` → room id and binds the anchor NPC (Tarko Vinn, placed in the warrens safehouse by the world build) by name. Best-effort: an unresolvable slug / absent NPC logs and leaves the contract unbound (the chain drives capture via `chain attempt` + `combat_won`, so this is quality, not a hard dependency).
- **Latent `bountytrack` crash fixed** (`parser/bounty_commands.py::BountyTrackCommand`): once the tutorial contract bound its target, `bountytrack` reached a line that called `Character.from_db_dict(char_row, skill_reg)` — but `from_db_dict` takes ONLY the row dict, so it crashed "takes 2 positional arguments but 3 were given". This command path was never reached before (it hard-errored earlier on the unbound target). Fixed the call; dropped the now-unused `SkillRegistry` import. Smoke `tests/smoke/test_smoke_chain_bounty_track.py` (CBT-1) drives claim → bountytrack end-to-end.
- **`examine` of room NPCs / objects** (`parser/village_trial_commands.py::ExamineCommand`): `examine <booth>` / `examine kost` / `examine crate` (republic_intelligence s2, smuggler s2, separatist_agent s2 examine steps) hit the flat "You see nothing special about X" even though their `command_executed` completion fired. ExamineCommand now delegates to `LookCommand._look_at` (after the fragment + inventory checks miss), reusing all the room-NPC / character / object / room_details resolution `look` already has — so `examine <npc>` renders the NPC's description + species, exactly like `look`. The generic not-found message is now `_look_at`'s "You don't see 'X' here." (E2 test updated to accept either wording). New E3 test (`tests/test_look_examine_inventory.py`) pins the room-NPC render.
- **Web onboarding panel: NEXT line + skill-step chip suppression** (`engine/chain_events.py` producer + `static/spa/m3_onboard.js` + `static/client.html` CSS): the step `next_hint` was authored in the corpus but never sent — now threaded through `get_active_step_info` + `build_onboarding_state` and rendered as a dimmer NEXT line under the OBJECTIVE. On `skill_check_passed` steps the descriptive `teaches` tokens (scan/search/sneak/etc.) are no longer rendered as clickable chips — they aren't actionable; only the ATTEMPT (`chain attempt`) chip renders, the one command that advances the step. JS verified in jsdom (`tests/spa/test_m3_onboard.py` — 2 new tests; the SPA DOM suite was unblocked on this box by installing jsdom at C:/tmp/node_modules). Browser eyeball still Brian's.
- **Test-isolation fix** (`engine/bounty_board.py::reset_bounty_board` + `tests/harness.py` boot): the bounty board is a process-level singleton whose in-memory `_contracts` survived across class-scoped harness boots — a chain bounty spawned + CLAIMED by one test leaked into the next test's board, where the idempotent-spawn check skipped respawn and the next test saw a stale CLAIMED contract. The smoke harness now resets the board at boot (same model as the world-events `_manager` reset). This is what let the new bounty-track smoke + the chain walkthrough's bounty_hunter test coexist.
- **Files:** `engine/chain_missions.py`, `engine/chain_events.py`, `engine/bounty_board.py`, `parser/bounty_commands.py`, `parser/village_trial_commands.py`, `static/spa/m3_onboard.js`, `static/client.html`, `tests/harness.py`, `tests/test_look_examine_inventory.py`, `tests/test_onboarding_state.py`, `tests/spa/test_m3_onboard.py`, `tests/smoke/scenarios/chain_bounty_track.py` (new), `tests/smoke/test_smoke_chain_bounty_track.py` (new), `CHANGELOG.md`, `TODO.json`.

---

### 2026-06-12 — Onboarding reachability coverage net + 3 chain-blocker fixes the net caught — *same-day drop 25*
Closes `TD.ONBOARDING_CHAIN_REACHABILITY_COVERAGE`. Drop 24 made all 7 chains *structurally* completable but shipped with no test that proves a player can walk one from a real chargen — every prior chain test injects state, pre-supplies destination slugs, or pre-places the player at a slugless room so the reachability gate short-circuits. This drop adds BOTH coverage layers the handoff specified, and in building the runtime layer it caught **three real production blockers** that drop 24's structural fixes didn't cover — each would have stranded a real player mid-chain.
- **P0.1 — static reachability invariant** (`tests/test_chain_corpus_reachability_invariant.py`, new, pure-YAML, ~1.6s): for every UNLOCKED chain, asserts four regression classes — (1) every room ref (`starting_room` / `graduation.drop_room` / `step.location`) resolves to a loaded room slug (the inter-step teleport strands the player otherwise); (2) NO `room_entered` / `item_acquired` completions (producerless in exit-less teleport rooms — consolidates + extends the inline `room_entered` guard in `test_f8c2b_chain_events.py` to also cover `item_acquired`); (3) every completion `command:` and `requires_first[].command` resolves through the REAL command registry, built by importing the server's `register_*` sequence (the guard that would have caught drop 24's unregistered `+factions`); (4) every `skill_check_passed` `skill:` / `fallback.skill` resolves via `canonical_skill_key` against `data/skills.yaml` ∪ the sanctioned `_FALLBACK` attr map (would have caught `starship_repair`/`starship_piloting`). Each class proven to FAIL on an injected regression.
- **P0.2 — per-chain walkthrough smoke** (`tests/smoke/scenarios/chain_walkthrough.py` + `tests/smoke/test_smoke_chain_walkthrough.py`, new; parametrized over the 7 unlocked chains): walks each chain from its REAL starting room to graduation using ONLY player-issued `cmd()` calls, asserting at EVERY step that the player is already standing in the step's authored `location` (the reachability gate — the exact assertion that was failing for bounty_hunter at step 3) BEFORE driving that step's completion. HARD RULES enforced: never calls a chain-event hook, never writes the next room_id, never injects chain state mid-walk — movement must come from the product (the inter-step teleport). New harness helpers `start_chain` (places the PC in the chain's real starting room with step-1 state, NOT room 1) + `room_slug_by_id` (`tests/harness.py`). All 7 walk green.
- **BLOCKER 1 — `chain_enemy_template` silently dropped** (`engine/npc_loader.py::_build_ai_config`): the ai_config whitelist preserved `is_intel_handler`/`skills`/`gate` but NOT `chain_enemy_template`, so every combat-template NPC loaded with the tag = None — the `combat_won` hook (`parser/combat_commands.py` ~L396) reads that tag to match the defeated enemy, so republic_soldier s2, separatist_commando s2, and bounty_hunter s4 could NEVER advance for a real player. Added the pass-through (same silent-drop class the `is_intel_handler` comment already documents).
- **BLOCKER 2 — tutorial combat rooms classified SECURED** (`data/worlds/clone_wars/tutorials/rooms.yaml`, additive): `tipoca_combat_sim` (Kamino) and `geonosis_foundry_drill_pit` (Geonosis) inherit SECURED zones, so `attack` was refused with "Heavy security patrols this area" — the drill couldn't run. Added `properties.security: contested` to both (sanctioned drill arenas; warrens safehouse was already LAWLESS). Purely additive (zero deleted lines).
- **BLOCKER 3 — multi-enemy `combat_won` unwinnable by natural play** (`engine/chain_events.py::on_combat_won` + `engine/tutorial_chains.py`): a step with `enemy_count: 2` (republic_soldier s2, separatist_commando s2) can't be met in one combat because the paired drill enemies don't aggro together — attacking one pulls only that one in, so the player fights them in TWO separate combats, each firing `on_combat_won(count=1)`, never reaching 2. Rather than rework combat AI, added a cumulative-kill tally on the chain-step state (`record_combat_kills`/`get_combat_kills`, keyed by template, cleared on step advance alongside `step_progress_satisfied`): two sequential count=1 wins now sum to 2 and the step advances. Accumulation only fires when the defeated template matches the active step's `enemy_template`, so unrelated combats never pollute it.
- **Test-only:** the walkthrough's talk driver polls for advance after `talk` (the chain hook fires from `_post_talk_hooks` AFTER the NPC's AI dialogue generation, which in the harness has no Ollama and falls back over ~3s — past the default cmd() quiet-window; a real player is unaffected). Combat driver clears transient PC stun/wound between swings so combat RNG can't strand the reachability walk (survivability has its own smoke). Bounty driver uses `bountyclaim chain_<id>`; give-prereq builds `give <item> to <npc>` so both `target_contains` AND `target_npc` substrings satisfy the prereq matcher.
- **Files:** `engine/npc_loader.py`, `engine/chain_events.py`, `engine/tutorial_chains.py`, `data/worlds/clone_wars/tutorials/rooms.yaml`, `tests/harness.py`, `tests/test_chain_corpus_reachability_invariant.py` (new), `tests/smoke/scenarios/chain_walkthrough.py` (new), `tests/smoke/test_smoke_chain_walkthrough.py` (new), `CHANGELOG.md`, `TODO.json`.

---

### 2026-06-12 — Tutorial-chain onboarding playability: all 7 starter chains completable (F.8.c.2.e) + `give` command — *same-day drop 24*
Live-testing a fresh Bounty Hunter surfaced that **all 7 unlocked tutorial chains were non-completable** — not one broken quest. Root cause (verified, multi-agent audit + adversarial re-derivation against HEAD): tutorial rooms have no exits (rooms.yaml EXIT POLICY) on the promise the state machine relays the player between step rooms, but that teleport existed ONLY for graduation — players stranded at the first step whose `location` differed from `starting_room` (the reported bounty_hunter step-3 strand). Two further independent blockers: the graduation step of all 7 chains completes on `command_executed: +factions`, but only `+faction` was registered (registry prefix-match fails on the longer string → "Huh? Unknown command" before the chain hook fires); and 2 `room_entered` steps are unreachable in exit-less teleport-only rooms. The whole tutorial test+smoke layer missed it by injecting chain state / pre-supplying destination slugs / pre-placing the player at a slugless room — never walking a real chargen through the registry.
- **Inter-step teleport (the keystone):** `engine/chain_graduation.py::apply_step_teleport` (resolve next step's `location` slug → `save_character(room_id=...)` → stamp `pending_step_room_id`); called from `engine/chain_events.py::_try_advance`'s non-graduation advance branch. `execute_pending_teleport` now serves BOTH the graduation flag (terminal flavor + reward summary, priority via key-presence classify) and the inter-step flag (light "you make your way" arrival). Failure-tolerant: an unresolvable slug logs WARNING and leaves the player put rather than stranding them worse. `engine/tutorial_chains.py` loader hardened so a `null` step location loads as `""` (not the literal `"None"`).
- **`+factions` graduation fix:** aliased `+factions` onto the `+faction` umbrella (`parser/faction_commands.py`). Bare `factions` deliberately NOT aliased — it would run the command but `ctx.command="factions"` wouldn't match the `+factions` completion (a silent "did the step but didn't advance" trap); locked out by test.
- **`give` command (NEW):** `parser/builtin_commands.py::GiveCommand` (`give`/`hand`) — one-way item hand-off to a PC (immediate transfer) or NPC (consumed; the Smuggler chain's `give crate to Dyn` rides the standard command hook). CREDITS deliberately route through `trade` (consented + 5% tax sink) — a one-way untaxed credit give would be a mule/laundering channel — so `give … credits` redirects. Anti-dupe: removes from giver FIRST, adds to a PC recipient with a compensating rollback (`add_to_inventory(..., fire_chain_hook=False)` — new kwarg in `db/database.py` so a rolled-back give can't false-advance a giver on an item_acquired step). Self/absent-target guards. Smoke `tests/smoke/test_smoke_give_command.py` (5).
- **Corpus fixes (`data/worlds/clone_wars/tutorials/chains.yaml`):** republic_soldier s4 + smuggler s3 `room_entered` → `talk_to_npc` (Pilot CT-7567 / Captain Reggi Voss, confirmed spawned in those rooms via npcs_drop_f8c2a); phantom skills `starship_repair`→`space_transport_repair`, `starship_piloting`→`space_transports` (the originals silently rolled raw Perception); shipwright s3 producerless `item_acquired: capacitor_coil_t1` (phantom `+craft fetch`) → `command_executed: +craft` with the coil as a step reward; misleading npc text across ALL chains (scan/search/sneak/bluff/follow/board/depart/stun → `chain attempt` / real verbs) and every dead-end directional `next_hint` ("type east/up/out") rewritten to describe what actually advances. `room_entered`/`item_acquired` are now unused by any chain — guard tests added so they can't reappear without a deliberate producer/reachability decision.
- **Global `look`/`examine <carried item>`** (separate confirmed bug): `LookCommand._look_at` only matched room contents; `examine` was holocron-only. Added a shared `_describe_inventory_item` helper (inventory + equipped items, descriptions from the item dict / EQUIPMENT_CATALOG) wired into both `LookCommand` (`parser/builtin_commands.py`) and `ExamineCommand` (`parser/village_trial_commands.py`), after the room match misses. Test `tests/test_look_examine_inventory.py` (6).
- **Web chargen tooltips:** `data-tip` on the template/species/ability cards in `static/chargen.html` (the SPA's existing delegated tooltip engine surfaces the full text on hover; truncation kept). Needs a browser eyeball.
- **Verified:** invariant-auditor (clean bar hygiene), smoke-verifier (boots clean, 216 smoke), code-reviewer (2 MAJOR + 1 MINOR found and fixed: give-rollback acquire-hook, `is_graduation` room-0 edge, teleport-failure log level). ~370 unit + smoke green across the touched surface; cascading test pins for the changed completion types updated (the room_entered/item_acquired dispatch tests now pin dormant-but-safe behavior).
- **Files:** `engine/chain_graduation.py`, `engine/chain_events.py`, `engine/tutorial_chains.py`, `parser/faction_commands.py`, `parser/builtin_commands.py`, `parser/village_trial_commands.py`, `db/database.py`, `data/worlds/clone_wars/tutorials/chains.yaml`, `static/chargen.html`, `tests/test_f8c2e_interstep_teleport.py` (new), `tests/test_look_examine_inventory.py` (new), `tests/smoke/scenarios/give_command.py` (new), `tests/smoke/test_smoke_give_command.py` (new), `tests/test_f8b_tutorial_rooms.py`, `tests/test_f8c2b_chain_events.py`, `tests/test_f8c2b2_chain_events_phase2.py`, `tests/test_f8c2b3_chain_missions.py`, `CHANGELOG.md`, `TODO.json`.
- **Note (map-safety judgment):** chains.yaml edits replace lines (a broken completion block can't be fixed additively). The "world YAML purely additive" invariant is read here as scoped to MAP/coordinate YAML (golden-snapshot of exterior surface rooms), not gameplay corpus — edits were comment-preserving string replacements, not a yaml round-trip rewrite.

### 2026-06-12 — Coruscant Underworld walkable: route custom wilderness edge directions — *same-day drop 23*
`PARSER.custom_edge_directions` resolved (option b, data-driven). `CommandParser.process` routed only a hardcoded compass + enter/leave set to MoveCommand, so a wilderness region edge declaring a CUSTOM `direction_from_room` word (the Coruscant Underworld's `deeper`) hit "Unknown command" — the region was reachable only via the synthetic `_drop_into_wilderness` test path (surfaced by the drop-21 underworld smoke). The dispatcher now merges in a data-driven set: `engine.wilderness_movement.get_custom_edge_directions()` harvests every edge `direction_from_room` from the region YAMLs (cached, boot-warm, independent of region-cache state; reset by `clear_region_cache`). New regions/edge words auto-route on the next boot — no per-direction code edit. MoveCommand's `_try_wilderness_entry` already matched arbitrary direction strings, so the dispatch gate was the whole gap.
- **Verified:** new `tests/test_parser_custom_edge_directions.py` (9) pins the harvest (`deeper` present, comment-line mentions excluded, lowercased, cache reset) + the exact dispatch routing predicate (compass + `deeper` route; non-directions don't). 203/203 across the wilderness + combat-wilderness + parser-command suites (run with the drop-22 `SW_MUSH_HARD_EXIT=1` workaround).
- **Files:** `parser/commands.py` (`_MOVEMENT_DIRECTIONS` const + data-driven dispatch), `engine/wilderness_movement.py` (`get_custom_edge_directions` + `clear_region_cache` reset), `tests/test_parser_custom_edge_directions.py` (new), `CHANGELOG.md`, `TODO.json`.

### 2026-06-12 — Test-suite exit-hang FIXED (run_all_tests.bat finishes cleanly) — *same-day drop 22*
`run_all_tests.bat` wrote its summary then HUNG — the `python -m pytest` process never returned, so the run had to be Ctrl+C'd and orphaned pytest processes piled up. Diagnosed (orphaned-process audit + a completed-but-hung log) as a process-EXIT hang, not a hung test: the run completes (`8333 passed`) but the interpreter won't exit, and the 120s pytest-timeout cannot catch an exit hang. A post-pytest `threading.enumerate()` audit named the culprit: leaked **aiosqlite worker threads** — aiosqlite spawns one NON-DAEMON `threading.Thread(target=_connection_worker_thread)` per connection (`aiosqlite/core.py:90`), and any test that opens a `Database` without closing it leaves that thread alive (blocked on its op-queue), blocking interpreter exit. `test_cities_phase4b` alone leaked 15 such threads.
- **Root fix:** `tests/conftest.py` marks every aiosqlite connection thread daemon at import time (a `Connection.__init__` wrapper sets `self._thread.daemon = True`), so a leaked connection can no longer block exit — the interpreter exits naturally with full teardown. Proven: `test_cities_phase4b` + the harness smoke files (all previously hung) now return rc=0 on their own (`26 passed`, no `SW_MUSH_HARD_EXIT`, no timeout-kill).
- An interim env-gated `os._exit` band-aid was added and then **removed** once the daemon fix proved out. `TEST.exit_hang_leaked_resource` → resolved.
- **Residual (hygiene-only):** the underlying connection leak (tests not closing their `Database`) remains — but the worker threads are now daemon, so they're reaped at exit. A later pass could close them in teardown.
- **Files:** `tests/conftest.py`, `run_all_tests.bat`, `CHANGELOG.md`, `TODO.json`.

---

### 2026-06-12 — Smoke-coverage restoration (6 loops) + 2 confirmed bug fixes — *same-day drop 21*
Audit (Brian's prompt: "is smoke discipline maintained?") found smoke had drifted to a catchup-batch cadence — recent drops shipped strong unit pins but no end-to-end smoke driver (the recurring "Pending: smoke it live" notes). The suite itself was green (192 passed) but frozen at the `big_catchup` commit. Restored coverage for the most-drifted player loops with **6 new in-process scenario modules** under `tests/smoke/`: `mission_loop` (board→accept→`mission`→complete reward→abandon), `buy_vendor_gate` (open-market vendor-presence + stock gates), `craft_trainer` (Gundark `learn` tuition), `commissary_loop` (rank-gated `tracking_fob` buy + `skill_bonus` in the inventory blob), `smuggling_loop`, `underworld_loop` (Coruscant Underworld region loads + exploration verbs). Full assessment + prioritized gap matrix in `docs/design/HANDOFF_smoke_coverage_gap_2026-06-12.md`.
- **Two confirmed bugs the new smoke surfaced — both fixed here:**
  - **Mission persistence** (restart-only impact): board ids are `"m-"+uuid` strings but `accept/complete/abandon_mission` did `UPDATE … WHERE id=?` against `missions.id INTEGER PK` → silent 0-row writes; accepted missions lost on restart. Fixed to match by the string id in the JSON `data` column (`save_mission`'s idiom) + upsert on accept. `mission_loop` ML2 asserts `get_active_mission` now persists. (`MISSION.persistence_id_mismatch` → resolved, option b.)
  - **Smuggling board unreachable** (total, live): `_in_board_room` read `ctx.session.current_room`, a phantom attribute never assigned anywhere → AttributeError → board dead in the live server. Fixed: `async def` reading the room via `ctx.db.get_room(char["room_id"])` (the established idiom); both call sites awaited. (`SMUGGLING.board_current_room_phantom` → resolved, option a.)
- **New gap filed** (surfaced by `underworld_loop`): natural wilderness entry into `coruscant_underworld` is blocked — `CommandParser.process` routes only standard compass words to `MoveCommand`, not the region edge's custom `deeper` direction. The scenario uses the synthetic `_drop_into_wilderness` pattern and flags it (`PARSER.custom_edge_directions_not_routed` → design_calls_pending_brian).
- **Verified:** full smoke `-m smoke` green; 69 mission + 80 smuggling unit tests green; touched modules compile clean.
- **Files:** `tests/smoke/scenarios/{mission_loop,buy_vendor_gate,craft_trainer,commissary_loop,smuggling_loop,underworld_loop}.py` + their `test_smoke_*` entries (new), `db/database.py` (accept/complete/abandon_mission), `parser/smuggling_commands.py` (`_in_board_room`), `docs/design/HANDOFF_smoke_coverage_gap_2026-06-12.md` (new), `CHANGELOG.md`, `TODO.json`.

### 2026-06-12 — Crafted weapon quality + boosts reach combat (Option B) — *same-day drop 19*
The consumer wiring gap is closed: previously `_resolve_equipped_weapon` in `parser/combat_commands.py` called `equipment_keys(...)["weapon"]` (key only) and looked up the registry `WeaponData.damage`, discarding the equipped `ItemInstance`'s quality and `effective_mods` entirely. A q100 thrice-experimented blaster was combat-identical to a q50 vendor one. Now `_resolve_equipped_weapon` reads the full instance (`read_equipment`), calls the new funnel `crafted_combat_pips(inst)` → `(dmg_pips, acc_pips)`, and folds the damage delta into `default_damage` via `apply_damage_pips` (DicePool carry/borrow automatic). The accuracy pip is captured as `accuracy_bonus_pips` on `CombatAction` (a new int field, defaulting to 0) and applied in `engine/combat.py::_resolve_attack` after the aim-bonus block, before the ranged/melee dispatch.
- **Numbers (WEG-faithful, hard-capped):** quality band {≤49: −1 pip, 50–69: 0 (vendor baseline), 70–89: +1, 90–100: +2}; damage_mod boost = `floor(damage_mod / 2.0)` capped +1, never negative; combined damage cap +3 pips (= +1D), floor −1. Accuracy: `floor(accuracy_mod / 2.0)` capped +1 pip to the attack pool. Max crafting investment buys +1D damage / +1 pip to-hit over a vendor weapon — a real sink-justifier that never beats a tier jump.
- **Backward-compatible:** vendor/legacy weapons (q50, no mods) yield (0, 0) from `crafted_combat_pips` — zero delta, unchanged behavior. Explicit `damage <dice>` override attacks are intentionally unbuffed (the `damage == default_damage` guard — same as Drop D's consume-block guard — ensures the bonus only applies when the equipped weapon is actually in play).
- **Armor soak deferred** (Option C) — blocked on `TD.EQUIPMENT_CHARACTER_HOLDS_KEYS_NOT_INSTANCES`: `get_armor_protection` holds only the key string; the equipment-instance migration must land first.
- **Combat isolation preserved:** `engine/combat.py` still never calls `perform_skill_check` (Drop F pin intact). The accuracy pip is a captured `int` read off the action, not a live equipment re-read inside the resolver.
- **Funnel discipline:** all quality→pip math lives exclusively in `_quality_band_pips` / `crafted_combat_pips` / `apply_damage_pips` in `engine/items.py`. No ad-hoc math at call sites.
- **Files:** `engine/items.py` (+`_quality_band_pips`, +`crafted_combat_pips`, +`apply_damage_pips`), `engine/combat.py` (`CombatAction.accuracy_bonus_pips` field; `_resolve_attack` pip add), `parser/combat_commands.py` (`_resolve_equipped_weapon` now returns 4-tuple; `_declare_and_broadcast` wired), `tests/test_obs_quality_combat.py` (new, 43 tests — pure helpers, integration, guard/isolation pins; Drop D + Drop F suites remain green).
- **Design calls:** `OBS.quality_and_boosts_not_combat_read` moved from `design_calls_pending_brian` to `design_calls_resolved_recent`. Ratified forks: combat-isolation breach for equipped crafted gear is sanctioned (different seam from the carried-tool isolation); +1D cap chosen.

Handoff item 4. The Coruscant Underworld 40×40 single-level region (8 design-doc anchors, `T2.3` DONE) is built out with **12 secondary landmarks** filling the grid beyond the anchors — authored in parallel by four `content-author` agents, one per disjoint quadrant, into **four new `landmark_includes` files** (no merge contention; coordinate-placed with no adjacency, matching the existing anchor pattern, NOT Dune Sea's adjacency-chained Village).
- **The four quadrants:** **NW** `coruscant_underworld_nw_overflow.yaml` — industrial/commercial overflow under Uscru (warehouse row, thoroughfare market w/ a small jobs hub, sublevel pump station). **NE** `_ne_smuggler.yaml` — smuggler reaches consistent with Factory Dominus (derelict loading docks, contraband transfer point, stripped cargo-lift hub). **SW** `_sw_deepwarren.yaml` — deep underlevels (ancient pipe market, foundation-stratum ruins, the lethal Null Gallery). **SE** `_se_mazefringe.yaml` — the Maze's lethal periphery (last ward marker, collapse gallery, shriek-dark sublevel). All era-clean (B3), Q1-canon-safe, original NPCs only.
- **Validated:** the full merged region loads through `engine.wilderness_loader.load_wilderness_region` with **0 errors / 0 warnings / 20 landmarks**, all coordinates and ids unique and in-bounds. Quadrant-disjoint coordinate assignment made cross-author collision structurally impossible; `nw_`/`ne_`/`sw_`/`se_` id prefixes guarantee unique ids.
- **What's consumed now vs. forward-looking (honest scope):** each landmark materializes into a **reachable, described room** (name + description + short_desc + terrain + `wilderness_landmark`) — the player-facing payload, consumed today by `wilderness_writer`. The `ambient_lines` pools ride the **pre-existing** `TD.WILDERNESS_AMBIENT_LINES_DEAD_WRITE` (written to a room prop with no runtime reader yet — affects the 8 existing anchors identically; surfaces when that TD is fixed). The gameplay properties (`threat_tier`/`gameplay_role`/`faction_anchor`/`low_level_warning`/`cartography_unstable`) have **no live consumer** — they reuse only the established anchor vocabulary (no invented keys) as forward-looking metadata for the encounter-spawner phase. **Not introduced here:** the wilderness map renderer is still hardcoded to Dune Sea (design §4a generalization, JS/SPA, Brian-Windows/browser pass) — the region's data is complete but renders as sand until §4a ships.
- **Tests:** `tests/test_coruscant_underworld_buildout.py` (9 — region loads clean, 20-landmark count, the 12 build-out ids at their exact assigned coords, coords in-bounds + unique, no invented property keys, not force-resonant, descriptions/ambient present, production strings B3-clean). No existing count-pin flipped (verified: nothing loads the real region and asserts an 8/9 count). `test_e3_data_era_cleanness` + `test_laneb_era_cleanness` green over the new files.
- **Files:** `data/worlds/clone_wars/wilderness/coruscant_underworld.yaml` (4 additive include lines), `coruscant_underworld_nw_overflow.yaml` + `_ne_smuggler.yaml` + `_sw_deepwarren.yaml` + `_se_mazefringe.yaml` (new), `tests/test_coruscant_underworld_buildout.py` (new), `CHANGELOG.md`, `TODO.json`.

### 2026-06-12 — Triage: city-tax buy tests vs the vendor-presence gate (watch item #7) — *same-day drop 17*
Pre-existing red fixed (found while verifying drop 16; confirmed red on the pre-session base commit 3c33074 — predates drops 13-16). `tests/test_cities_phase4b.py`'s three `BuyCommand` city-tax tests (`TestBuyCmdInCityTaxed`, `TestBuyCmdOutsideCity`, `TestBuyCmdPlayerAccountingUnchanged`) were written before **`ECON.vendor_presence_gate`** (drop 11, prior session) made `buy` refuse unless an NPC with `ai_config.vendor:true` is in the room. With no vendor seeded, `BuyCommand` early-returned with "No merchant here sells weapons" **before** `apply_city_tax` ran, so the city's `revenue_total` stayed 0 and the purchase message never printed — exactly the HANDOFF §7 watch-item #7 flip ("buy gates on vendor presence").
- **Resolution: fix the tests, not the gate.** Added a `_seed_vendor_npc(db, room_id)` helper (uses the canonical `db.create_npc` seam with `ai_config_json={"vendor":true}`) and seeded a vendor in the room for all three buy tests, so they exercise the real purchase + city-tax path the gate now requires — rather than asserting the OLD ungated-buy behavior. `TestBuyCmdOutsideCity` previously passed only trivially (the blocked buy left revenue at 0 for the wrong reason); it now buys successfully outside any city and meaningfully asserts no city take. The weapon the tests pick (`hold_out_blaster`, the first cost>0 non-armor) is `vendor_stocked`, so the drop-10 stock gate is satisfied; only the vendor-presence gate was blocking.
- **No production/data change.** Test-only. File is 16/16 green; cities/buy blast radius 158/158 green.

### 2026-06-12 — Triage: T5-difficulty invariant vs the Drop G contraband band — *same-day drop 15*
Pre-existing red fixed (found while verifying drop 14; confirmed red on HEAD before drops 13-14, unrelated to either). `tests/test_syn6c_t5_crafting_and_harvest_nodes.py::test_t5_difficulties_are_above_t4_ceiling` asserted every `t5_*` schematic out-ranks the *dynamic* max difficulty of all non-T5 schematics. That invariant predates **Gundark Drop G**, whose contraband band (`predator_rifle`, `anti_vehicle_grenade` @ diff 26 — the Heroic cap, the catalog's "worst pages") legitimately reached the same difficulty ceiling via a **different axis** (illegality / experimental-prototype danger), not crafting tier. So three T5 rows (top_spec_blaster_rifle 25, master_grade_armor 25, hyperdrive_surge_converter 26) failed a strict `> 26` test.
- **Resolution: fix the test, not the data.** The contraband difficulties are correct per Drop G's rubric; the T5 difficulties (25-28) are correct per their design; only the test's assumption that the two never collide was stale. The test now **excludes `contraband` schematics** from the ceiling, preserving a strong, meaningful invariant: every T5 difficulty exceeds the hardest *legal* non-T5 recipe (max legal = `comm_jammer` @ 24; all T5 ≥ 25 ✓). T5 is the hardest lawful crafting lane; the contraband band is a deliberately-extreme separate category.
- **No data/balance change.** Test docstring rewritten to document the axis distinction. 40/40 in the file green.
- **Files:** `tests/test_syn6c_t5_crafting_and_harvest_nodes.py`, `CHANGELOG.md`, `TODO.json`.

`T2.DEF.t5_drop_hooks` fully closed. `scavenged_republic_tech` now faucets from Coruscant Underworld harvest via a region-keyed, tier-independent 7% bonus roll (+1 stack @ q75), reusing the existing `compute_harvest_payout` → `add_resource` path with no new system. ### 2026-06-12 — Vendor-presence gate: vendors ≠ hagglers — *same-day drop 11*
`OBS.buy_verb_followups (a)` resolved as **decision a + vendor flag** and delivered. Buying open-market commons now requires an NPC with **`ai_config.vendor: true`** in the room — the `trainer: true` precedent applied to commerce. This deliberately disentangles VENDORS from mere HAGGLERS: the old haggle scan grabbed the first Bargain-skilled NPC in the room (Lup the grocer was an implicit arms dealer; a random cantina tough could set your price), and with nobody present a phantom "generic 3D vendor" closed the sale anyway — the deep desert sold blasters. Now: no flagged vendor → "No merchant here sells weapons. Find a shop." — and the haggle reads **the vendor's own** Bargain (generic 3D only when the flagged vendor lacks the skill), fixing the first-Bargain-NPC bug as a side effect.
- **Curated vendors — every major settlement gets a buy point:** Kayson + Sela Tarn (Kayson's Weapon Shop), Lup (General Store), Jawa Trade-Elder Ruzz-tha (Jawa Traders) — Mos Eisley · Trex Hovan (Lower City Black Market) — Coruscant (flagged in the era-loaded `southern_underground` file; the `_lower` duplicate is dead data) · Halen Korr (Weapons Cache) + Reska Tol (Undercity Market) — Nar Shaddaa · Sela Dorne (Stalgasin offworlder camp) — Geonosis. **Kamino deliberately has none** (faction world; the commissary serves it). **Gundark is NOT a vendor** — he teaches the contraband band, he doesn't retail commons; knowledge is the only cargo the patrols can't confiscate. Pinned.
- **The uncurated-vendor sweep test** walks every CW NPC yaml: a `vendor: true` outside the curated set fails loudly, so future vendors are curation decisions, not side effects.
- **Tests:** `tests/test_econ_vendor_presence.py` (7 — curated flags present; curated files era-loaded; Gundark-not-a-vendor pin; uncurated sweep; gate-refuses source pin; haggle-uses-the-vendor pin; old-loop-gone pin). Sandbox: 15 econ + 117 adjacent green.
- **Files:** `parser/space_commands.py`, 7 NPC yamls (additive `vendor: true` lines), `tests/test_econ_vendor_presence.py` (new), `CHANGELOG.md`, `TODO.json`.
